Economic Supplement

Trends in Rose's Work in China 154

— Sen Yu

Before Rose arrived in Shanghai, the author predicted in issue 142 of this publication that Rose's key objectives in China would be fourfold: (1) to consolidate past loans and investments, (2) to provide new, independent loans to China, (3) to bring China into the Sterling Area, and (4) to establish a foundation for dealing with Japan. Observing Rose's recent words and actions, what he has expressed directly and indirectly seems to align quite well with our previous speculations. Therefore, we will further examine Rose's work trends from an objective perspective:

(1) Consolidating Past Loans and Investments

This item seems less important in Rose's work and is largely passive. Therefore, most people have not paid much attention to it. However, we believe that this issue is by no means a simple "debt collection problem," but rather contains the significance of consolidating the British economic front in China. Historically, British loans and investments in China have often been secured by important tax revenues and railway interests, with the actual control of China's customs and salt taxes largely in British hands. Recently, Japan, the United States, and others have been attempting to squeeze out Britain's superior position, especially Japan's ambition to seize customs rights, which has become more active. To maintain the strength of its fortress, even if Britain does not intend to demand repayment of debts from China, it must use the name of consolidation to deploy its new front. Rose's recent collection of information, especially focusing on China's debt situation and tax revenues, is likely to prepare for a comprehensive and thorough reorganization of Sino-British debt relations. On the one hand, this means presenting a list of debts to China, but on the other hand, the main purpose is to re-establish clearly the "debt collateral" to prevent other countries from coveting it.

However, according to our observation, the work of consolidating past Sino-British debts and investments is quite heavy and may not be completed in the short term. As for this economic front, if there are no other forces to protect it at the same time, it will still be vulnerable under Japan's drastic measures. The previous examples of the Beining Railway and the Kailuan Coal Mine can serve as clear lessons.

(2) Providing Independent Loans and Investments to China

(1) Collateral for Loans Rose once told reporters about the issue of loans to China, saying, "It depends on the nature of the collateral." This indicates that loans to China must be conditional, and the so-called "collateral" will obviously further involve China's economic sovereignty and financial administration. Rose's special emphasis on China's debt situation and tax revenues, as mentioned above, is also a preparation for finding new collateral. The main target of this collateral is undoubtedly China's tax revenues and other state-owned enterprises (railways, mines, etc.)'s income. If a Sino-British loan agreement is indeed established and secured by a certain tax revenue or state-owned industry, Britain will further manipulate China's tax affairs and state-owned enterprises in the name of supervision and auditing. As a result, Britain will not only directly control China's financial lifeline but also indirectly promote the favorable development of trade and investment.

(2) Private Targets for Loans and Investments Rose is well aware that negotiating with the Chinese government will be subject to various constraints and may not be smooth. It is also necessary to engage in various agreements with private groups and individuals outside the government, and China's financial and industrial circles are the best targets. Rose's meetings with leaders of Shanghai's financial and industrial circles in recent days are not without this important intention.

(3) Main Direction of Investment The North of China may not have room to intervene, the Northwest is not smooth, and the Central region also has many constraints. Although the Southwest has recently been threatened by Japan and will conflict with France, it is still the best option in a situation where there is almost no other choice. Moreover, with Hong Kong by sea and India by land, it is easier to enter and exit. Therefore, the current center of British activity in China seems to be in the Southwest (naturally, it does not absolutely abandon the Central and Northwest regions; activities are still carried out within the possible scope). Rose's recent work also seems to focus on this area, and the actively progressing major transportation network plan in the Southwest provinces is an important step to lay the foundation. Secondly, operating in the Southwest is not only the foundation for entering and exiting China, but also plays a huge role in the future world structure. When the Southwest, India, Burma, Hong Kong, and even Singapore are integrated, the British position in the Pacific will take a superior position.

The above three items are the main trends of British activities in raising loans and making new investments. The final decision of their future will depend on the evolution of the future international situation and China's final attitude. However, according to our current speculation, we dare not be fully optimistic for Britain: (1) The collateral for loans affects China's financial sovereignty, which will be opposed by the Chinese people, and will inevitably arouse the jealousy of international imperialism, especially Japan, and hinder it; (2) Although investing in China's private sector is more likely to succeed, it is expected that it will also arouse resentment from the United States and other countries and must overcome many difficulties; (3) Japan has recently stepped up its expansion into the Southwest, and the power of France cannot be underestimated. Therefore, Britain's operation in the Southwest will at least cause a three-way confrontation between Britain, Japan, and France, and various accidents will occur.

(3) Persuading China to Join the Sterling Area

Although Rose avoids mentioning persuading China to join the Sterling Area, he has stated that he will conduct detailed research on China's economy, especially its currency system, which provides some clues. Moreover, objective facts show that this work is a necessary part of Rose's visit to China. The reason why he is so secretive is to avoid various constraints.

Recently, some financial figures have been vocal about China joining the Sterling Area, and there have been proposals to immediately link Sino-British exchange rates, which is indeed a matter worthy of attention. They believe that the root cause of China's economic panic at this stage lies in the excessive silver exchange rate and the contraction of currency, ignoring other political and economic fundamental factors and placing all the responsibility for the panic on the currency, which is putting the cart before the horse. We feel that after China joins the Sterling Area, it will lose its independent monetary sovereignty (some people think that the issue of sovereignty is only nominal and not important in practice; if so, then the entire national sovereignty can also be considered only nominal, and it may be okay to give it away casually. I wonder if this is acceptable). Moreover, the exchange rate will fluctuate with the pound, and there is still no possibility of stability. This kind of vassal-like development will make China's economic panic even more serious. Some people say that the Japanese yen is also related to the pound and has not caused any harm. Therefore, they hastily conclude that China joining the Sterling Area is harmless and beneficial, which is extremely absurd! The relationship between the Japanese yen and the pound and China's joining the Sterling Area are inherently different in nature. Even if the natures are the same, I wonder if China and Japan have the same national status? In short, China's joining the Sterling Area has more disadvantages than advantages, and we dare not welcome it.

As for the international impact of China joining the Sterling Area, it will be very serious and need not be repeated. The strong opposition from the United States and Japan is inevitable.

(4) Establishing a Foundation for Dealing with Japan

Regarding Sino-Japanese relations, Rose may continue to try to coordinate with Japan. However, there is little hope, and even if possible, it is only within a very narrow limit. Japan's ambition will never make Britain feel at ease. Therefore, on the one hand, Britain has to seek ways to resist. It is estimated that his work mainly has three aspects: (1) using international forces to prevent the expansion of Japanese power, (2) uniting to resist Japanese aggression, and (3) broadly establishing a foundation for dealing with Japan at all levels of China's economy and politics. However, (1) international relations are complex and not absolutely reliable; China's current strength is too weak, and there are too many constraints; as for (3), such as seizing China's financial power, monetary power, and operating in the Southwest, etc., are all strategies for both offense and defense, but unfortunately, there are too many obstacles.

Above, we have summarized and analyzed the various tasks that Rose has done, should do, and will do in China this time. As the objective situation shows, the results may not be entirely as Britain hopes. However, it cannot be absolutely certain that nothing will be achieved. The following items may be more likely to be gained: (1) A deeper understanding of Japan's ambition can be a very important lesson for the British government; (2) The information obtained from the investigation and study of China's economic situation can be good reference materials for the British government; (3) The past debt relationship between China and Britain may be able to agree on a principle of consolidation; (4) Several cooperative enterprises may be established in the private sector; (5) If a loan is established within a certain limit, some benefits may be obtained on railways and mining. Among the above items, (1) and (2) are no problem; but (3) is still far from reality and needs to be discussed again in the future; as for (4) and (5), they are only "possible" and still need to overcome multiple obstacles. The recent tension in the European and African situation and Japan's general mobilization of its China policy will make Rose's work more and more difficult!

Review of the Land Village Ownership System 155

— Chen Honggen

The land issue has always been a central issue in politics. In primitive societies, land was originally public. By the Three Dynasties, it evolved into the Well-Field System. After Qin Shi Huang unified the world, the private ownership system was established, and the concentration of land increased daily, which greatly affected the relations of production in society. Therefore, after each dynasty's political changes, the victors invariably took the reform of the land system as the most urgent task, using it as a slogan to stabilize the people's hearts. Most of these reforms aimed to prevent the concentration of land ownership. The most popular ones were Wang Mang's Royal Land System during the Wang Mang period, the Bai Xing Land Occupation Law of the Western Jin Dynasty, the Equal-Field System of the Later Wei Dynasty, the Eternal Property and Naked Land System of the Sui Dynasty, the Hereditary Portion System of the Tang Dynasty, and the Limited Restriction System of the Song Dynasty. However, few of them were effective, and in the end, almost all of them abandoned their policies, and the land returned to the path of private concentration. Since the Ming Dynasty, the facts and degree of annexation have become increasingly severe. From the Qing Dynasty to today, there has been no thorough remedy. According to reports, Yan Xishan of Shanxi Province advocated the land village ownership system to prevent the spread of the Red Disaster. Its main points are:

(1) The village office issues public bonds to collect all the land in the village for public ownership.

(2) The land is divided into several plots according to its nature and distributed to the villagers for cultivation.

(3) Farmers receive and return the land at the beginning and end of their cultivation age. If there are too few land and too many people or too much land and too few people, it will be adjusted by immigration.

(4) The public bonds for buying land are repaid with income from industrial property protection tax, income tax, and non-labor tax.

Mr. Yan's advocacy of this method has a very far-sighted vision, and in principle, it is indisputable. However, in view of the past experience of land reform success, certain unavoidable difficulties will inevitably be encountered in practice. I hereby contribute three opinions on this method within my humble knowledge, and I dare not decide whether they are right or wrong, just for the reference of the people of the country.

(A) The Problem of Scarcity and Unevenness of Cultivated Land China's farmers today are generally suffering from a shortage of cultivated land, but there is no exact proof of how much it is insufficient. According to the results of the survey conducted by the National Government's Accounting Office in 1933, each household has an average of 2.1 acres of cultivated land. Mr. Zhang Xinyi estimated that each person has 3.6 acres of cultivated land. Cressy estimated that each person has 0.4 acres of cultivated land. Baker estimated that each household has 2.85 acres of cultivated land. The survey of 13 places in Jin Dalu Province showed that each household has an average of only 2.52 hectares. The United States has an average of 3.6 acres of lower land per day, which is about nine times larger than China, and each household has 57 acres of cultivated land, which is about 18 times larger than China. In the case of China's small cultivated land area, we found that there is no large-scale concentration as in foreign lands. Therefore, the core of today's land distribution problem is not the re-division of already cultivated land, but the area of arable land that has not been cultivated. According to Mr. Weng Wenhao's estimate (Cone Finger Collection), the area of arable land in China is one million square miles. Baker estimated that it is 700 million acres, which is too high. According to the survey conducted by the National Government's Accounting Office in 1933, the area of cultivated land is 1,248,781,000 acres, which is about 189,814,72 acres. However, the actual number is definitely more than this, because some cultivated land is not reported for tax avoidance purposes, so it is difficult to be accurate. Zhang Xinyi's food source survey in 14 provinces stated that except for the four northeastern provinces, the expansion of cultivated land area in the other nine provinces is unlikely to exceed 5% of the existing cultivated land. The implementation of the Well-Field System was due to the sparse population and abundant land, so it was still possible to measure and distribute land according to the population, as Gou Yue said (quoted from Tong Kao, Volume 1): "Moreover, the Well-Field System is not suitable for times of large populations. When land is vast and people are few, it is feasible." Therefore, in today's time of heavy population, the difficulty of implementing the land distribution system must be greater than that of the Well-Field or Equal-Field System in the past. The possibility of expanding uncultivated land is so small that it is not allowed by facts to make the land distribution system last for a long time.

(B) The Amount of Fertile and Barren Land Varies from Village to Village Yan's proposal is to distribute land to villagers according to the land in each village. The first problem is that villages have sizes, and the distribution of land is still not equal. Some people think that small villages have less land and fewer people, and large villages have more land and more people, which is fair. In fact, the area of villages in the South is mostly smaller than that in the North, and the population density is higher than that in the North, which can be seen from the difference between population density and land distribution. According to Mr. Yan's proposal, if the land in the village is not enough to distribute, then people without land will find a way to make a living, or move into villages with surplus land to adjust it. This is common practice under the current private land ownership system. If the land is made public and given to the people, then who would not want to have land to cultivate and live in their hometown, and would rather go out to make a living. Especially in our country, with a strong sense of family and hometown, unless there is the oppression of natural disasters and man-made disasters, no one is willing to leave their hometown easily, so the result will inevitably lead to some disputes. In terms of the quality of soil, fertility is different. If it is forced to be divided into several plots, then everyone will inevitably compete for fertile land. As Sheng Ruzhi said in "Shuzhai Laoxue Congtan," the strangeness of the terrain, the unevenness of the soil, and the unevenness of water and drought are all difficulties in dividing the Well-Field. According to Zhou Guan, the number of fields received by each husband is not limited to one hundred mu, as Mencius said. As Da Situ said, "Use the method of soil equalization to distinguish five things and nine grades to determine the land of the world, levy it to make people's taxes, order land tribute, verify wealth, and equalize the politics of the world." Therefore, there are two types of land distribution systems in the Zhou Dynasty. "In the countryside, the upper land is one chen per husband, and the field has mu? Lai fifty mu, and the rest of the husbands are the same; the middle land is one chen per husband, and the field is one hundred mu, and Lai is one hundred mu, and the rest of the husbands are the same; the lower land is one chen per husband, and the field is one hundred mu, and Lai is two hundred mu, and the rest of the husbands are the same." "In the cities, families that are not easy have one hundred mu, families that are easy once have two hundred mu, and families that are easy twice have three hundred mu." This distribution method is just to make it tend to be average, but in fact, the handling must be very complicated. Now, if the land of a village is granted to the villagers, if it is not graded, then it is not as fair as the Well-Field. If it is to be graded, then its complexity is unavoidable.

(C) The Difficulty of Re-Dividing According to the provisions of Article 13 of the Village Public Ownership Plan, the public office should re-divide the plots at appropriate intervals according to the increase in population and the land improvement situation. This is easy to say but difficult to do. Unmarried farmers must continue to reach the age of cultivation to apply for land, and at the same time, there are constantly elderly farmers returning land to the village office. This matter of granting and returning land is extremely heavy. If it is accumulated for several years or ten years before re-division is carried out once, then what will the farmers who have reached the age of receiving land do before the re-division? Moreover, for those who have already received land, they have been guarding their land for several years. If they are asked to cultivate other land, they will be unwilling to improve their land or exhaust their land before re-division. Therefore, after several years, the productivity of the land must be greatly reduced, and the situation of the farmers has not improved. The reason why the Equal-Field System of the Northern Dynasties, Sui, and Tang could not last for a long time was partly due to the disorder of the land registration book, which eventually led to the land being granted without being equal. The lessons of the past can be learned. Now, how will it be corrected?

(D) About the Village Office All land surveying, population registration, and land distribution matters are handled by the village office. Then, the person in charge must have received considerable training in the above matters to avoid errors. Today's rural education is so naive that most farmers do not know what land public ownership is. In addition, the village office may not have the necessary knowledge and experience to handle land distribution matters, which may arouse farmers' suspicions that the government is plotting to seize their land, which will ultimately be fruitless or even lead to farmers' resistance. Moreover, the villagers are of mixed quality. Some of them are local bullies and ruffians who have no land to stand on, but they get land because of this. At the same time, some lazy and extravagant farmers who have lost their land ownership also enjoy the same opportunity. Ordinary diligent farmers who originally had dozens of acres of land and had a well-to-do family may not only fail to improve their situation after the land is heavily levied, but may also suffer losses. This phenomenon is especially prone to occur in areas with low tenant rates. Moreover, local bullies and ruffians often collude with local tyrants and gentry to control the village office. All land distribution procedures are handled by them, and fertile land is allocated to themselves or their relatives for cultivation, and the remaining inferior land is distributed to others.

(E) About Income Tax All those who receive cultivated land must pay one-tenth of their income as labor income tax as part of the guarantee for the repayment of public bonds. Mencius said, "The Xiahou clan paid tribute at fifty, the Yin people helped at seventy, and the Zhou people used Che for one hundred mu. In fact, all of them were one-tenth." Later generations were confined to the saying of one-tenth and competed to make associations, some said that it was due to the difference in the urgency of the government, and some said that it was due to the difference in the length of the ruler, and there was no consensus. Now, if the farmers who receive land are also required to pay one-tenth of their harvest, is it fair? The fertility of the land is unequal, and the yield per mu is different. Under today's tenancy system, rent and grain are all based on the yield per mu, and the percentage of the rent and tribute paid by both parties varies greatly, with so-called split halves, three-sevenths, four-sixths, two-eights, etc., all aiming to balance the interests of both parties. Now, if a uniform labor income tax of one-tenth is levied, then the burden on farmers who cultivate good land and farmers who cultivate inferior land cannot be balanced.

(F) Can Public Land Ownership Permanently Prevent Annexation? Today, most of the larger landlords have a considerable relationship with the local politics. Even if they are temporarily ordered to release their land, they cannot prevent the matter of forced sale. The farmers' land is annexed by the powerful, but they still have to bear the taxes. This can be seen from the implementation of the Equal-Field System in the Northern Dynasties, Sui, and Tang Dynasties, as Mr. Yu Guoding said, "The Equal-Field System equally grants good land, but the number of fugitive households is the highest in the Northern Dynasties, Sui, and Tang Dynasties, which implemented the Equal-Field System... The Western Han Dynasty did not grant people land but levied rent per mu, so the household tax was lighter. Since the implementation of the Equal-Field System, the land rent has also been levied per household, so the household tax has greatly increased. However, the granting and receiving of land is only carried out when the politics are clear and there are many people with few land. When the compliance is temporary and the name is not real, the powerful annex land and the poor lose land. The officials do not grant land again, but the heavy taxes cannot be reduced again, so they become a serious disease for the people and flee together, not because they are sick of having land, but because they are fleeing heavy taxes."

The above points are about the discussion of the land village ownership system itself. In addition, there are several more basic problems, which are also listed below.

(A) Public or Private Land Ownership, Which is More Beneficial? It has been said before that land originally belonged to the public in primitive times, but the result of social evolution has universally created a phenomenon of private ownership. The successive formation of this trend is not accidental, and there must be the impetus of its background. Because private ownership and possession are the nature of human beings, since the establishment of the private ownership system, individuals have been willing to work hard to seek the enrichment of their own pockets. The economic and cultural progress of society is also based on this. Since the development of individualism and free competition in Europe, the progress of industry and commerce has been rapid. Most of the transportation and other public utilities in the United States today are operated by private individuals, and their efficiency and spirit of service are no less than those of state-owned enterprises, and their motivation is to focus on self-interest. Therefore, whether land should be public or private is a question that should be carefully considered.

(B) Today's Land Problem or the Entire Agricultural Problem is Not Limited to Distribution Aspects As mentioned, the land use problem is also extremely important. Today, Chinese farmers invest a lot of manpower in land. Compared with the United States, the production of cotton per hectare in China requires 1,620 hours of labor, while the United States only needs 289 hours. Sorghum in China requires 637 hours, while the United States only needs 48 hours. The situation of other crops is the same. (According to Buck's survey of Chinese farmhouses and the statistics of the 1921 US Agricultural Yearbook) Although China uses a lot of manpower on land, its output is still not as high as that of other countries. According to Tawney's research (Land and Labor in China), the yield of rice per mu in Japan is 2,350 pounds, while China is only 1,750 pounds. The yield of wheat per mu in England and Wales is 32.9 bushels, while China ranks ninth with only 10.8 bushels. The yield of corn is the highest in the United States, at 27.8 bushels, while China ranks sixth with 11.7 bushels. From this, it can be seen that the effectiveness of today's Chinese agricultural workers is far less than that of other countries. Therefore, if we improve the means of production on a limited area and increase the yield per mu, it will also greatly improve the lives of farmers. Other aspects such as agricultural finance, agricultural product marketing, rural education, and hygiene need to be thoroughly reformed, and we cannot ignore them. By starting simultaneously from various aspects, the recovery of China's rural economy can be expected.

(C) The Crisis of Using Agriculture as the Basis for Supporting the Population "Relying on agriculture to build the country" has almost become a cliché among the Chinese people. This sentence can indeed represent China's past or present economic situation. However, whether we can continue to rely on agriculture to build the country in the future is a question that needs to be considered. Most of the irrigable land in mainland China has been exhausted. The irrigable land in the future is limited to several places on both sides of the Yellow River and the three northeastern provinces. According to experts, even if agriculture is scientifically implemented, its output is unlikely to exceed the existing 20% to 50%. At most, it will only temporarily slightly improve the living standards of farmers. After a considerable period, it will inevitably return to the previous state of poverty. Most of the major powers have now moved from agricultural civilization to industrial civilization, and large factories have absorbed the surplus population, making the land distribution problem easier to solve. There are several difficulties in China's industrialization at present. First, there is a lack of financial and human resources. Second, there is a shortage of minerals and power raw materials. Third, it is not easy to compete with other countries in the world market. As a result, it is still ineffective. Therefore, we can only seek the simultaneous development of agriculture and industry at present. On the one hand, we should promote the country's industry to a considerable extent, and on the other hand, we should strive to improve agriculture, so as to adjust the shortage of cultivated land and stabilize the foundation of the country's economy.

Finally, we admit that seeking land distribution reform in China today is not meaningless. It can solve the livelihood problems of the people to a considerable extent. Public land ownership is not absolutely impossible. If there is a very detailed plan that can overcome the various difficulties of the previous public ownership system, it will have great value. Therefore, we hope that the proponents can continue to study its theory and implementation steps so that the village public ownership system can truly achieve the goal of liberating farmers.

Finance The Expiry Date Was Amicably Resolved 156

—The next two periods will be handled in the same way—

Yesterday (the 21st), the situation regarding the maturity of long-term debts on the 10th was very tense. The debtors always attributed their inability to repay to the market situation, making rollovers inevitable. However, creditors, in order to protect their own interests and avoid risks, had to try to contract. As a result, the gap was still significant. A general overview was detailed in yesterday's report. All Chinese banks had largely agreed on this the day before yesterday (the 19th) after much effort. The details of most of the transfers were also detailed in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday was a Sunday, and most banks were closed, so the arrangements were made a day in advance. As for the long-term loans owed to and from money shops, although some matured the day before yesterday, a considerable amount was cleared yesterday after several negotiations. Of the total amount of over 7.7 million, 3 to 4 million was settled yesterday by both parties. It is said that the terms of the adjustment were difficult to accept. However, the Chamber of Commerce had sent a letter to the Money Trade Association, asking for amicable handling. For debtors who genuinely had unavoidable difficulties and could not repay as desired, the request was reluctantly granted, allowing rollovers. Therefore, creditors did not dare to demand too much, and the situation was resolved where possible. Those that could not be collected were rolled over. However, the interest rate was 5 jiao higher than the market rate, hence the market price of 9.5 to 10 yuan. The long-term loans from Ningbo banks in Shanghai were also negotiated several times, with less than 50,000 to 60,000 being recovered. The remaining large amounts of long-term debts were all rolled over at the request of the Chamber of Commerce. Therefore, the total transaction volume yesterday was no less than ten million or more. As for the two major expiry periods (the 25th and the end of the month) that have not yet arrived, the amounts are very large. We predict that the outcome will be no different from yesterday's. However, some of the more solid debtors may be able to repay, but most of them will have uncollectible receivables due to accounting relationships, and it is inevitable that they will request rollovers. Looking back at the foundation of the money shops themselves, after the Ministry of Finance issued financial public bonds, and with the gradual contraction of business, the adjustment of capital can also be managed smoothly, and there will be no major crisis. Moreover, a few money shops have had shareholders add additional capital, so the overall situation does not seem to have any impact. However, new customers are not being given loans, and stores that want to rely on the financial sector for assistance feel very difficult. Before the end of this month, it is inevitable that some stores will be unable to maintain operations and will declare liquidation. We hope that our predictions are incorrect.

Last week (October 14th to 19th), the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange market was still in turbulent waters. The supply and demand of market chips changed with the environment. People's sentiment was always weak. The big players, both bulls and bears, seemed to be quite firm on the surface, but in reality, they had mostly moved their positions imperceptibly. The sellers' preparation for delivery was indeed a fact. Given the large quantities on both sides, the barriers were extremely high. Even without environmental changes, the momentum of mutual friction would have been significant. Moreover, with only five days left before settlement, the swap operations of both the bulls and bears in recent days had been quite busy. It could be predicted that the changes within the day would still be quite remarkable. The environmental rumors were particularly absurd and terrifying. The rumors were more intense on Monday of last week compared to the previous week, and there was also news of war between Japan and Russia. Prices fell more and more drastically from morning to night. The Disbandment Bonds fell by 2.1 jiao. Number 16 was shorting heavily, and Number 54 was bullish. Number 16 was still shorting heavily, and the northern gangs were also pouring out, and the decline did not abate. New low prices continued to be discovered. Although it rebounded slightly at the end, it still fell by about 0.5 yuan. On Wednesday, the market conditions were unpredictable, and the selling pressure was still strong. Number 48, a long position, released a small number of shares. Number 16 continued to add to their short positions. There were a lot of rumors in the market. The situation between Britain and Italy was also gradually deteriorating. The Disbandment Bonds fell again by 1.75 yuan, creating a new low price. Thursday was the busiest day of trading. Transactions were only made in three sessions. After the first session continued to fall sharply, the financial community rose up to support the market, and the market price actually rebounded by 3 jiao to 1 yuan. On Saturday, there were still many rumors, and prices were quite different, about 3 to 4 jiao. Looking at the overall situation for the week, Number 16 was selling every day, and Number 48 was also mostly buying. Both sides were adding to their positions. Changes were coming, and the momentum was growing. The market price results for the week all declined, from 1.2 jiao to 1.15 jiao. The trading volume on Thursday was the smallest. The National Games Closed Yesterday Guangdong Swept Both Men's and Women's Swimming Championships China-West Track and Field Confrontation Created Two New Records Athletes from Various Places Left Shanghai One After Another 162

The sixth National Games, which were at their peak, came to a successful conclusion yesterday and were declared closed. The men's and women's overall championships were still retained by Shanghai. Guangdong won the men's and women's overall third place, and the men's overall third place should have been Ma Hua, but the conference listed it as fourth and instead listed Hong Kong as third. In the women's group, Shandong and Shanxi were tied for third place overall. Yesterday's final men's and women's swimming championships were swept by Guangdong, and two new swimming records were created. As for yesterday's China-West performance competition, it was quite moving for a time. In the track and field competition, two excellent new records were also discovered. The conference held a closing ceremony at 5 pm yesterday, and athletes from various units have scheduled their returns.

The Grand Occasion of the Closing Award Ceremony Telegrams of Condolence to Chairman Chiang Express Men's and Women's Championships Awarded Separately 163

The sixth National Games, which opened on National Day, has concluded all competitions. The closing ceremony of the conference was held after the completion of the international competition yesterday. At 5 pm, under the enthusiastic mood of 150,000 Chinese and foreign spectators, the ceremony was simple and grand. The closing speech was given by the President of the Conference, Mr. Wang Shijie, and awards were given by President Sun and Minister Kong respectively. The details are recorded as follows:

Telegrams of Condolence to Chairman Chiang

When the conference held the closing ceremony yesterday, it sent a telegram of condolence to Chairman Chiang of the Military Commission of the National Government in Nanjing, which read: "Chairman Chiang, Military Commission of the National Government in Nanjing, has been disturbed by the Red bandits for many years, and the country has been troubled many times, which has been extremely difficult. You, General Leader of the Division, commanded with determination, supervised the division in Jiangxi, went straight to the lair, drove north, gathered and annihilated Sichuan and Yunnan, held hair and vomited, worked hard and made great contributions, and all my compatriots admired it. The National Games were held in Shanghai, lasting more than ten days, with nearly 3,000 athletes from home and abroad, and more than one million spectators. Looking up to virtue and majesty, and yearning for demeanor, only you are diligent and worried, and have not been able to fulfill your wishes. Now, on the day of the closing ceremony of the conference, everyone unanimously sent a telegram to express their admiration and condolences. Please inspect it, Wang Shijie, Chairman of the Sixth National Games, Wu Tiecheng, Vice Chairman, and all unit general representatives, general team leaders, athletes, and all conference staff."

More Than 100,000 People Participated

Honorary Vice Chairman Kong Xiangxi, Sun Ke, Preparation Director Wu Tiecheng, Committee Members Wang Zhengting, Chu Minyi, Pan Gongzhan, Lei Zhen, Ma Chonggan, Jiang Jianbai, General Secretary Shen Siliang, and Advisors Huang Shaoxiong, Luo Jialun, etc., all participated in the grand event. Yu Hongjun presided over the ceremony. At 5 o'clock, the music was played to start the conference. The flags of 38 units were brought into the venue by the Boy Scouts and arranged in front of the West Command Platform. Behind them were the athletes of each unit, but most of them had left the conference, so there were only hundreds of athletes from Wei, Hai, Kang, Ha, Re, Hei, Ji, Liao, Ma, Gan, Hu, Yu, Ji, Jin, and other provinces. Various championship awards were displayed in front of the venue, dazzling and eye-catching.

President Wang's Closing Speech

After the ceremony, the Chairman of the Conference, Wang Shijie, delivered a closing speech, roughly saying: "Today is the last day of the National Games. Over the past ten days, representatives from various provinces and cities have competed in accordance with various procedures, which is very good. I believe that you all understand the main points of sports. There are three things I want to say today: (1) Maintain sportsmanship and athlete morality. Sports have educational significance and should be based on this purpose to seek the development of intelligence and moral education at the same time. (2) Encourage women's sports. In the past, our country did not pay attention to women's sports, but now it is gradually promoting it and the results are gradually appearing. I still hope that all representatives will continue to work hard. (3) The duration of this conference is longer than in previous years, and all facilities are quite perfect. This is enough to show progress, and the hard work of all preparation staff and all preparation committees should be deeply thanked. I wish you all a safe journey and continue to work hard in the sports industry to promote the physique of our nation." Chairman Chiang of the Military Commission is very concerned about this conference. Because Chairman Chiang is stationed in Sichuan to suppress bandits and has made meritorious service to the country, he specially sent a telegram of condolence, which was applauded and approved by the whole audience.

Awards Given for Championships

After the speech, the awards were given. The first prize for the men's and women's overall championship was Shanghai, awarded by President Sun. The first prize was Guangdong, awarded by Minister Wang. The third prize was Hong Kong, awarded by Dr. Wang Zhengting. The fourth prize was Malaya, awarded by Mayor Wu. The first prize for the women's overall championship was Shanghai, awarded by Vice President Kong. The second prize was Guangdong, awarded by Huang Shaoxiong. The third prize was Shandong and Shanxi, awarded by Secretary-General Chu. Other prizes will be collected at 10 am today.

Lowering the Conference Flag and Great Cheers

The conference flag was slowly lowered amidst the music. Then, Preparation Director Wu Tiecheng presented it to Minister of Education Wang Shijie for safekeeping. Thus, the sixth National Games, which mobilized hundreds of thousands of people for eleven days, came to an end. It was already dusk, and the lights were shining brightly. Athletes from various places left the venue one after another, and tens of thousands of spectators dispersed and returned.

Yesterday was the closing ceremony, with China-West football matches, and there were still many visitors, and more than 13,000 yuan of tickets were sold. It is said that the ticket money entrusted by the conference to the city bank and China Travel Service has not been completely paid. Last night, the conference calculated the ticket revenue to be about 110,000 yuan, more than twice the ticket budget of 50,000 yuan.

Tennis Championship Scoring Error 165

Both Men's and Women's Occurred Between Sichuan and Malaya 166

This Newspaper Has Corrected It and Requests the Organizing Committee to Re-Verify the Awards 167

According to the total championship scoring table issued by the organizing committee, in men's tennis, Sichuan was third and Malaya was fourth. However, based on the verified match results, Malaya won third place in doubles, and Sichuan won two fourth places in singles and doubles. Therefore, in the championship rankings, Malaya should be ranked third and Sichuan fourth. However, the organizing committee's announcement was exactly the opposite. At the very least, the two teams should be tied for third, with each receiving one and a half points. If this were the case, Malaya would be third in the overall championship standings with ten and a half points, and Hong Kong would be fourth with ten points. Now, Malaya is ranked fourth in tennis, which affects its overall championship ranking. The difference is slight, but the impact is significant. This is the first point that the organizing committee should pay attention to.

In women's tennis, Shanxi is undoubtedly first and Shanghai second. Nanjing won third and fourth place in singles, ranking third, which is also not a problem. Sichuan won third place in doubles and should be ranked fourth in the tennis championship. Although Malaya won fourth place in doubles, it was not enough to be ranked. However, in the total championship scoring table released by the organizing committee, Sichuan has no points, while Malaya is ranked fourth with one point, which is unknown on what basis. This is the second point that the organizing committee should pay attention to. In this competition, there was a previous error in the reversed rankings of sixth and seventh place in five sports. Because no one protested, it was glossed over. Fortunately, it was unrelated to the championship rankings and was a minor matter. Now, the difference in tennis scores is slight, but it is directly related to the championship rankings, which is extremely important. The organizing committee should carefully verify and announce the results based on the achievements to demonstrate credibility. This newspaper has already made corrections on their behalf and re-prints the situation of the men's and women's tennis championships as reported in yesterday's newspaper for reference.

Guangdong Wins Men's and Women's Swimming Championships 168

Hong Kong Men's and Women's Teams Take Second Place 169

All Women's Records Broken 170

Three New Men's Records 171

Yesterday's swimming competition, still began at 1:00 PM, with only three events, namely the men's 200-meter relay final, the men's 1500-meter freestyle final, and the women's 200-meter relay final. With that, all the swimming competitions came to an end. The Guangdong men's and women's teams scored the most points and each took home the championship trophy. Details are recorded as follows:

Men's 200 Relay The men's 200-meter relay final saw Shandong, Hebei, and Qingdao withdraw, so only eight teams from Pingma, Jiangxi, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Shanghai, and Hong Kong participated. Each team had four members. At the sound of the gun, Hong Kong and Guangdong took the lead, neck and neck. Until the very last leg, Hong Kong was slightly ahead of Guangdong, reaching the finish line in 2 minutes and 1 second and 2 tenths. But Guangdong also reached the finish line in 2 minutes and 1 second and 4 tenths, a difference of only two tenths of a second. Third was Malaya, fourth Shanghai, fifth Fujian, and sixth Guangxi.

Men's 1500 The men's 1500-meter freestyle final was truly one of the most intense scenes. There were eight participants. When they first entered the pool, Shanghai's Shi Bogen and Malaya's Yang Weimo took the lead. Before they had gone ten laps, Shi gradually fell behind. Hong Kong's Chen Zhennan, amidst thunderous applause, was able to keep pace with Yang Weimo. At this time, Guangdong's Mai Weiming, Guangxi's Huang Jinghuan, and Hong Kong's Chen Zhenxing were also neck and neck. By the 18th lap, Chen Zhenxing suddenly felt weak and uncomfortable and stopped swimming midway. Fujian's Hong Xun also stopped soon after. At this time, only six people continued swimming, and they all had the hope of winning a prize, so they all put in extra effort and moved forward vigorously. By the 25th lap, Yang Weimo even leaped ahead. Hong Kong's Chen Xiaonan was unwilling to show weakness and tried his best to catch up. Yang and Chen were already more than two laps ahead of the others. As a result, Yang was ultimately the better, and when Yang reached the finish line, Chen was still 20 meters away. Yang came first and Chen second, but their scores were 22 minutes and 59 seconds and 2 tenths, and 23 minutes 23 seconds and 1 tenth, both breaking the national record. Guangxi's Lei Bingchang, although ranked last, was not far from the fifth place. Fujian's Lei, at only fourteen years old, is truly a force to be reckoned with.

Women's 200 Relay The women's 200-meter relay final was the grand finale. Originally, there were five teams from Guangdong, Malaya, Fujian, Guangxi, and Hong Kong, but only three teams from Guangdong, Hong Kong, and Guangxi participated. The Hong Kong team had the Yang sisters, so they were most confident of winning the championship. Guangdong's Liu Guizhen, Chen Huanqiong, and others were also strong competitors and were unwilling to fall behind. After Hong Kong, Guangdong's Liang Yuzhen took the lead all the way, with Hong Kong's Chen Yuhui following behind. In the second leg, there was no difference between Guangdong and Hong Kong. In the third leg, Guangdong's young general Weng Huanqiong's swimming was slow, which was the main reason why Hong Kong later finished in second place. In the fourth leg, Guangdong's Liu Guizhen entered the water. When Hong Kong's Yang Xiuqiong entered the race, Yang Chong started sprinting with full force, but at the finish line, she was still about two meters short, finishing second. Third was Guangxi. The score for first place was Guangdong, 2 minutes 39 seconds and 2 tenths, breaking the national and Far Eastern records. Second place Hong Kong, 2 minutes 42 seconds and 7 tenths, also broke the national record. Third place Guangxi, 2 minutes 49 seconds, tying the national record.

Letter from Provincial Flood Relief Associations Requesting Disaster Relief Competition 172

The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces, in order to raise relief funds, sent a letter to the National Games requesting that a disaster relief competition be held. The original letter stated, "In reply, this association previously sent a letter to your association regarding the severe floods in various provinces and the urgent need for relief, requesting that the games be extended by three days, and the proceeds from ticket sales be used for disaster relief. We have now received a reply stating that the games are limited by expenses and restricted by the articles of association, making it difficult to extend the games. These are indeed real circumstances. However, fundraising for disaster relief relies on collecting small amounts to make a large sum. In addition, the weather is getting colder, and the need for funds is extremely urgent. Therefore, we once again plead on behalf of the disaster victims, hoping that you will consider the tragic situation in the disaster areas and, within the realm of possibility, select a few events that are of interest to all sectors, such as a football match, to help with disaster relief, in order to provide relief. We will be deeply grateful and hope to hear from you soon. To Mr. Wu, President of the Sixth National Games, and Vice President, from the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces."

Track and Field Competition: China Wins Big 173

Dai Shuguo Sets New National Record in 400 Meters 174

—51.6 Seconds—

Li Shiming Also Sets New Record in 800 Meters, Chinese Team Ties National Record in 400 Meter Relay

Yesterday's Sino-Western track and field competition was a contest between the outstanding athletes from this National Games and the Western expatriates in Shanghai. The Western athletes were a combined team from England, America, and Russia. As a result of yesterday's competition, the Chinese team won nine of the ten events. Except for the discus, where Guo Jie and Leng Peigen were absent and lost, the rest of the championships belonged to the Chinese. The full results are recorded below:

Event 1st 2nd 3rd 4th Result

200 Meters Liu Changchun (China) Dai Shuguo (China) Feng Sazha (West) Li Pidafu (West) 22.3 seconds

400 Meters Dai Shuguo (China) Li Yanxiang (China) Feng Sake (West) Like Kaonaf (West) 51.6 seconds (New)

1500 Meters Wang Zhenglin (China) Qiu Zhongcheng (China) Luo Wu'er (West) Aiyute Fu (West) 4 minutes 22.6 seconds

Dai Shuguo's Achievement is Commendable

Among yesterday's competitions, the most commendable was Dai Shuguo's 400 meters. Dai was the champion of the 400 meters in this National Games and set a new national record with 52.2 seconds. In yesterday's 400-meter race, Dai started very fast. Between 200 meters and 300 meters, he competed fiercely with the Westerner Like Kaonaf, with excellent speed. It seemed that he still had energy to spare after finishing the race. This was probably a major reason why Dai set a national record yesterday. Dai set a national record with 51.6 seconds, which can be said to be unprecedented. This record will be recognized as the national highhest record for 400 meters this year.

Liu Changchun Amazes the Audience

Liu Changchun won two championships in the 100-meter and 200-meter races, and the results of both were quite satisfying. In the first event, the 100-meter final, Liu Changchun led from start to finish, showing very strong strength. He is truly worthy of being the only short-distance prodigy in our country. Less than ten minutes after the 100-meter race, the 200-meter race began. Liu led all the way, throwing off second place Dai Shuguo by a large margin. The audience was amazed. The 100-meter and 200-meter races were both held against the wind, and the results were 11 seconds for the 100 meters and 22.3 seconds for the 200 meters. In particular, the result of the 200 meters was very close to the national record.

Hao Chunde Wins Two Championships

The veteran Hao Chunde, in this National Games, was like a dragon trapped on the beach. Due to eligibility issues, he was unable to compete. In yesterday's Games, he was finally able to show his skills. In the javelin throw, he won the championship with 49.129 meters, overwhelming Peng Yongxin, the champion of the National Games. Hao also won the championship in the long jump with a result of 6.63 meters, surpassing Ye Sui'an, the long jump champion of the National Games. In fact, Hao defeated two champions of this National Games yesterday. Mr. Hao is old, but his prestige still remains.

Li Shiming Loses One, Gains One

Li Shiming broke the national record in the 800 meters with 2 minutes and 4.2 seconds, but his result was not as good as the 2 minutes and 2.1 seconds of the champion of this National Games. Also, Li was the scorer in the javelin throw in this Games. Li's javelin throw yesterday was 47.815 meters, but it was not listed. It can be said that he lost one and gained one.

Many Famous Generals Return

In yesterday's discus final, we were missing two great generals, one was the champion of this year, Guo Jie, who returned to his hometown of Dalian the day before yesterday, and the other was the runner-up, Leng Peigen, who had already returned to Beijing. It was also rumored that Jin Cheng did not appear in the 100-meter and 200-meter races because he went to Hangzhou for sightseeing. Jia Yunren also gave up the 800-meter and 1500-meter races, reportedly due to poor health. Also, Wu Bixian, who once scored points in the high jump, was disqualified by the organizing committee this time. Although the organizing committee invited Mr. Wu to attend yesterday, Mr. Wu had actually returned to Tianjin four or five days ago. Yu Qingrong, who also did high jump, also returned home.

Detailed Description of the Competition

100

The first shot was fired, but the Westerners were recalled for a false start. When the second shot sounded, Liu Changchun started as agile as in the finals of the Games, followed by Zhao Bingheng. Liu led all the way and was two meters ahead of Zhao at 50 meters. He beat second place Ye Haitao by five meters at the finish. Ye and Zhao competed fiercely at 50 meters, and as a result, Ye finally surpassed and won second place.

200

The 200 meters was held immediately after the 100 meters. Liu Changchun did not run the 200 meters in the National Games, so this time he was determined to give it his all. Liu is highly respected in the sprint community in our country. For seven or eight years, no one has been able to break his records. Yesterday, in the 200 meters, Mr. Liu showed his strength, proving that Liu's reputation is well-deserved.

400

In the 400-meter race, only Li Yanxiang and Dai Shuguo from the Chinese team participated. Dai started the fastest. Between 200 meters and 300 meters, he competed fiercely with the Westerner Like Kaonu, but Dai ran faster and faster, and Li Yanxiang soon surpassed the two Westerners Fang Sake and Like Kaonu. At the finish, Dai beat second-place Li Yanxiang by about ten meters.

800

Jia Lianren did not appear in the 800 meters, and there was a lack of competition. Li Shiming remained in first place throughout, followed by Qiu Sicheng, followed by the three Westerners. Li Shiming ran casually and did not exert much effort from start to finish, rushing straight for the finish line, with a result of 2 minutes and 4.2 seconds, breaking the national record. Qiu Zhongcheng did not exert himself in the 800 meters and comfortably got second place, because he was still preparing to score points in the 1500 meters.

1500

Wang Zhenglin has recently tended to switch to middle-distance running, and the 1500 meters has become his forte. Wang Zhenglin started with a bold and unrestrained style, running with his familiar speed regardless of everything, leading all the way. The second place was the two Westerners, and Qiu was in fourth place. Wang Zhenglin ran faster and faster, and no one competed with him. Qiu was in last place, but he was confident and entered second place in the last 300 meters.

Long Jump

There were three great generals attending the long jump, namely Ye Sui'an, Zhang Jia夔, and Hao Chunde. Ye and Zhang's past results had all reached 7 meters, while the old Hao was the holder of the national record. None of the three Westerners who participated were worth mentioning. In the first week of trial jumps, there were no special performances. Hao got 6.63 meters on the fourth run, and Ye jumped 6.57 meters on the third jump. The results are as follows:

Women's Tennis Singles 175

Wei Maigu Ranked Runner-Up 176

Defeated Nanjing's Huang Shannong 2-1

The battle for the runner-up in women's tennis singles was held at 9:00 AM yesterday morning. Shanghai's Wei Maigu relied on her steady hitting skills, fought fiercely for three sets, and barely won 2-1. Huang was good at attacking, and Wei was good at defending. It was a pity that Huang made too many unforced errors and was defeated by Wei's soft approach. In the first set, Wei's momentum was strong, and she took the lead, winning three games in a row. Huang was also unwilling to be outdone and responded in kind, and each tied at four games. Wei continued her efforts and used the trick of feinting to the east and attacking in the west to exhaust the opponent, adding two games to win the first set 6-4. In the second set, Huang was still not in good shape and fell behind 4-2. At this time, the situation changed, and Huang suddenly cheered up, attacking rapidly with backhand and forehand strokes, and moving freely left, right, front, and back. Wei, on the other hand, ran around defending and was unable to serve. Huang won three consecutive rounds and took the lead 5-4. Next, when Huang served, she initially had the advantage with 40 to 15, but then her old problems recurred and she repeatedly made mistakes, creating a tie. But Huang was not discouraged and continued to work hard. Sure enough, where there is a will, there is a way, and she won two consecutive games to win back a set 7-5, forming a tie. The third set was decisive, but Huang had used too much energy in the previous set and was exhausted. Wei, on the other hand, was shining brightly and full of momentum, winning five games in a row in one go. Although Huang bravely resisted and won back three games, the overall situation was gone, and it was impossible to turn the tide. Wei finally won the final victory 6-3, ranking runner-up, and Huang ranked third.

The expenses for the trip to Beijing and other receptions have been decided to be borne by Beijing. Sino-Foreign Football Exhibition Match: China United and Western United Fail to Score, Ending in a Lackluster 0-0 Draw; Absence of "King of Football" Leaves Forwards Helpless in Front of Goal 179

Yesterday at 3:00 PM, the China United team, a mix of winning teams from the All-China Games football tournament, played against the Western United team, a mix of the strongest foreign football players in Shanghai. Our side was weakened significantly due to injuries to "King of Football" Li Huitang (arm), goalkeeper Bao Jiaping (back), and the absence of key players Xu Yahui, Chen Zhenhe, Sun Jinshun, and Zhu Jianjiang. The China United team was based primarily on players from Hong Kong and Malaya, with only Tan Jiangbai from Guangdong added. However, Tan's heading ability saved many dangerous situations. Western United's left and right wings were very active, and their defense was solid. The game ended in a 0-0 draw. The exhibition lacked tension and excitement. Although the China United forwards' passing was excellent, they lacked shooting ability. Cao Guicheng missed the most opportunities, wasting his efforts. If the "King of Football" had been on the field, victory would have been effortless.

Mayor Kicks Off

Yesterday at 3:20 PM, the game began with Mayor Wu kicking off. Cao Guicheng intercepted the ball and launched an attack toward the enemy camp. Two foreign defenders rushed to stop him, and Cao, in his eagerness, dribbled the ball out of bounds. Shortly after, center forward Xie Qingfu led a fierce attack, taking a long shot from 30 yards out, but the ball sailed over the goal. At the same time, foreign wingers Walter and Willie attacked from the left and right, but their shots were also ineffective.

Goalpost Obstructs

For the next 15 minutes, Western United launched an all-out attack with great intensity, constantly bombarding the goal. Fortunately, Huang Jinbai was experienced and composed, blocking the ball with hands and feet, not yielding an inch. The time passed back and forth until the 30th minute when our left inside forward, Li Zhaorong, received a brilliant pass from Cao Guicheng, dribbled past the final line of defense, and took a powerful shot at the goal. Unfortunately, the ball hit the goalpost with a loud thud and rebounded. Cao Guicheng intercepted the rebound but also missed. The foreign players cheered, while our team was dejected. At that moment, the whistle blew, ending the first half with a scoreless tie.

Following Suit

After the break, the teams switched sides and the Chinese team launched a fierce attack, dominating the enemy camp for over ten minutes. There were at least seven or eight scoring opportunities, but our forwards lacked precision and power. In addition, the experienced foreign goalkeeper was well-trained, resulting in wasted effort. The entire crowd sighed. In the 14th minute, our right inside forward, Yao Shenghua, fiercely dribbled the ball past defenders, employing a feint. The two foreign defenders thought Yao would pass to the right winger and rushed to intercept, but Yao seized the opportunity to kick the ball powerfully at the goal. The ball flew like a bullet, but again was blocked by the goalpost, following suit and bouncing back into our territory. It was both regrettable and infuriating.

Devoid of Excitement

Soon, the momentum shifted, and our side was under pressure again. The Western United forwards moved freely, with the left and right wings charging like a broken dam. Fortunately, Tan Jiangbai repeatedly showcased his heading skills, earning applause from the entire crowd. Otherwise, losing a goal at that crucial moment would have sealed our fate and been impossible to recover from. After the 20th minute, the game became chaotic, with high balls flying back and forth. The game became loose, lacking excitement. Finally, the game ended with the score still 0-0, demonstrating the spirit of friendship. The entire crowd smiled and quietly observed the closing ceremony.

Sino-Foreign Women's Basketball Match: China Heavily Defeated by Western United; Score of 51-12; Western United Hardly Able to Retaliate 180

After the international men's basketball match, the Sino-foreign women's teams took to the court. The Chinese team was the Shanghai Women's Basketball Team, champions of the All-China Games, also known as the Liangjiang Women's Basketball Team. Western United was based on the formidable Green Team, with additional outstanding players from other teams. Yesterday's game was almost entirely dominated by the Chinese team, with Western United hardly able to resist. The Liangjiang team had been defeated by the Green Team in last year's Western Youth Women's Basketball Tournament, demonstrating the team's significant improvement. However, Western United used men's rules, employing a six-player, two-zone system, which may have contributed to their defeat. After the center jump, Chen Jucai scored two consecutive baskets within a minute, and Bai Naite also scored two points. Chen Rongming dominated the court, and the enemy's basket was repeatedly threatened. Chinese fans smiled with joy, while the blonde-haired foreign players sighed. The first quarter ended 11-5, giving the foreign ladies a warning. In the second quarter, Pan Meng scored, and Rongming scored again. Western United only scored one point from a free throw by Basake. The first half ended with a decisive 17-6 victory for the Chinese team. After drinking lemonade, the Chinese team saw that Western United was not a strong opponent, so Chen Rongming and Jucai declared their retirement, and Wan Shunxiang and Chen Rongtang took over their roles. Western United began to rally slightly, with Rowling scoring two baskets and Bai Naite also scoring. Before time ran out, the Chinese women's team achieved a great victory.

Sino-Foreign Tennis Exhibition: Xu Chengji Loses to Carson; Exhaustion from Consecutive Matches Leads to Defeat; Lin and Xu Team Up in Doubles to Defeat Devoe and Carson 181

Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Chinese and foreign tennis stars held a grand exhibition at the All-China Games tennis court, competing in three matches, all played in a best-of-three sets format. In the end, Carson defeated Xu Chengji 2-1 in singles, Qian Yaobin defeated Forbes 2-0, and Xu Chengji and Lin Shihua defeated Carson and Devoe 2-0 in doubles. All matches were exceptionally exciting, especially the Carson-Xu singles match. The results are as follows:

Xu Chengji Loses to Carson

The Xu-Carson match began at 10:15 AM amidst thunderous applause from the audience. Xu is a national player, while Carson is the Shanghai singles champion. The two are evenly matched, and the outcome depended entirely on their performance during the match. When Xu and Carson returned to Shanghai after participating in the Davis Cup in the United States, they competed once in Shanghai, with Xu winning 2-1. However, Xu had been competing in the All-China Games for several days without rest, inevitably leading to exhaustion. After winning the first set 6-1, his energy waned, and Carson seized the opportunity to defeat him 2-1, which was a pity.

Full of Excitement

Carson's serve faltered, and Xu took advantage, gaining a 2-0 lead, seizing the initiative. Carson fought back hard, winning a game. Xu continued to press, with great momentum. His low and fast cross-court shots were precise, and Carson scrambled left and right, unable to defend effectively. Everything went smoothly, and Xu won four consecutive games, winning the first set 6-1 with ease. In the second set, he was cautious and did not dare to be careless. Each point won required considerable effort, making the match full of excitement. The applause thundered. Both players countered with low and fast cross-court shots, or used lobs to challenge their opponent. However, Carson was tall and strong, exceptionally agile. Xu showed a slight lapse, and Carson seized the opportunity to take a commanding 5-1 lead. Although Xu fought hard to regain a game, Carson won 6-2, tying the match at one set apiece.

Missed Opportunity

The final set was the key to victory. The match became increasingly intense and exciting, with each player giving their all for every point. The audience watched with bated breath, completely focused. However, Xu missed opportunities at crucial moments, while Carson became increasingly courageous and ran quickly. Even when faced with the most difficult shots, he refused to give up. The outcome depended on this. At the beginning, the two sides were evenly matched, keeping pace with each other, and the score remained close, 2-2, 3-3, and then 4-4. Xu was leading the way, and in the ninth game, Xu served, immediately committing a double fault, followed by an unforced error. He lost the game. In the next game, Carson served, and Xu initially had a 40-30 lead, but his desire to win led to more unforced errors, while Carson responded carefully and calmly, winning three consecutive points and taking the set 6-4.

Qian Yaobin Defeats Forbes

The Qian Yaobin vs. Forbes match began around 11:00 AM. Forbes is the Shanghai junior singles champion, with admirable skills. Qian had defeated strong opponents in the All-China Games, and his forehand shots were sharp and fast. After the start, Forbes took the initiative, winning three consecutive games. Qian refused to be outdone and retaliated, coming from behind to lead 4-3. Forbes tried again, tying the score at 4-4. Qian rallied and won two more games, winning the first set 6-4. In the second set, Qian became even more dominant, hitting high and low shots at will. Forbes collapsed and struggled to defend, only winning one game in the entire set, losing 6-1.

Lin and Xu Pair Well in Doubles

Xu and Lin paired for the first time to face Carson and Devoe, who were considered invincible in Shanghai. After a dramatic two-set match, they won with a very close score, which was no easy feat. Overall, Lin Baohua was the most outstanding performer. Xu, exhausted from the singles match and in a poor mood, inevitably showed signs of fatigue while facing strong opponents. Although he occasionally made excellent plays, he was not as energetic as Lin in the overall match. Carson and Devoe were similar in style, and their ability to save difficult shots was amazing. Devoe's overhead smash sometimes had unpredictable landing points, but he also made many mistakes, unlike Carson, who was more steady.

First Set

Xu started serving, and Lin Baohua's three delicate and beautiful volleys at the net won the first game. After that, Xu and Lin frequently used high-pressure skills, quickly taking a 4-0 lead. Carson and Devoe pulled back two games, but Xu and Lin also won, making it 5-2. Carson and Devoe fought desperately, rushing to save even the most difficult balls. Once, Carson fell into the crowd sitting on the edge of the court while saving a ball, showing his effort. Therefore, they finally caught up with three games, making it 5-5. They then exceeded with 6-5. Xu and Lin responded cautiously and also won two games, leading again 7-6. Carson and Devoe also created a 7-7 tie. Xu and Lin cheered up, hitting two baseline cross-court shots and winning the game 9-7.

Second Set

Carson and Devoe took the first three games with an extraordinary momentum. The audience worried about Xu and Lin, but Xu and Lin were not weak. With a similar burst, they formed three games creating equilibrium. Then go to 4-3 exceeded. Devoe's serve failed, and again to equal. Xu and Carson serve are winning into 5-5, Lin and Xu hard to deal with one and again save the dangerous ball. Devoe high pressure and the self-destructive net lost a game. Xu and Lin came to be, winning the forest with 7-5, Xu and Lin Kai triumph

Result: 3-3

The exhibition match of little football between Hong Kong and Shanghai began at 10:00 AM on the 2nd, refereed by Shu Zhongguang. Both teams were full of talent and had similar strengths. Before the match started, the stands around the small football field were packed with people, estimated to be over ten thousand, the largest crowd seen for a little football match. The two sides then formally engaged, fighting fiercely for an hour, resulting in a tie. The intensity of the match was self-evident. The details of the battle are recorded as follows:

First Half: 2-2

Therefore, Bian Fangyi sought to be the first, and was eager to desperately sandwich the merit. Within more than 20 minutes, the match was difficult to resolve. In an instant, the time was up, and the match ended in a 3-3 tie.
