Post-Games Impressions 188

Encouraging Football Players

In this session of the Games, the football championship had four major teams competing: Hong Kong, Malaya, Guangdong, and Shanghai. Their strengths were balanced and each had their own advantages. It was truly the most exciting football tournament in the history of the Games. Our country has always held the top position in football in the Far East, and society is particularly interested in football. In the last few days, the track and field was packed, all football fans watching the games. The future development of football is limitless. This time, there were eighteen units participating in the competition. Except for Qinghai, which withdrew due to insufficient personnel, the rest all held a courageous spirit of resistance and fought to the end, which is most admirable. The teams from Hebei, Liaoning, Nanjing, Beiping, Hubei, and Qingdao had been trained for a long time, and their strength was already considerable. Others, such as Fujian, Anhui, Henan, Shandong, Jiangxi, and Hunan, had not participated in large-scale battles before, and were hastily formed. However, they emerged unexpectedly, and their skills were amazing. For example, Fujian fought Shanghai, Henan fought Nanjing, Shandong fought Guangdong, Sichuan fought Beiping, and Anhui fought Hong Kong. Facing strong enemies, they were able to fight hard and performed extremely well. The difference in scores was not something to criticize. If they are given time and training, they will become strong teams. When we meet again in the next National Games, we should look at them with new eyes after three days of separation. As for the four teams of Hong Kong, Malaya, Guangdong, and Shanghai, they are a collection of football talents in our country. The division of competitions is to increase practice, excitement, and develop experience and courage. Do not be concerned about the championship issue and stand apart. It is important to know that unity within the country can lead to resistance and victory against external forces. The World Games in Berlin next year are approaching. I sincerely hope that all football players will return and work hard, dedicating themselves to serving the country on the world football field and striving for supreme glory. Returning home with honor will be the true meaning of the training in today's National Games competition.

Shortcomings in Tennis

The advantages and disadvantages of the new system for the tennis championship have already been proven. What is the use of blaming? Everything must be successful through experimentation. Then we can use this to plan for the best possible method in the future. Therefore, today's poor system is nothing more than a new creation in the future.

The abolition of the Davis Cup system in this session was originally for the significance of attached grading competitions outside the team championship. Therefore, the allocation of order was like an open competition, producing both individual and team championships at the same time. The purpose was to improve domestic tennis technology and increase the interest of players, because our country has never held grading competitions. We took this opportunity to seek a win-win solution. However, because of the lack of careful planning in advance, there were shortcomings and things went wrong.

In the new system, doubles is no longer a problem. Singles, because there is a distinction between the first singles and the second singles, and the ranking of the first and second places is classified and arranged, is the biggest mistake. For example, if the first and second singles were mixed and arranged, this problem might not have occurred.

After understanding the principles, we should strive for thoroughness and become a purely open competition. After the final champion is resolved, the ranking of each player should be reviewed to determine the team to which they belong. Then, the team ranking should be judged. If so, it will not only comply with the principles of the grading competition, but the team championship will also be produced accordingly.

Assaulting Referees Still Occurs

In today's Games, athletes under certain authority often act arrogantly and cause trouble. Referees are humiliated and the organizing committee treats it lightly. Referees have become the target of their wrongdoing. The Hangzhou Games started this trend, and it has been seen again and again in Nanjing and this year's Games. Referees are beaten, and nothing is done about it. The organizing committee has no response. Those who are directly affected can only swallow their anger for the sake of face, while there is no response to the athletes who act arbitrarily. How can this arrogant atmosphere be quelled?

The Issue of Athletes Competing in Multiple Events

The competition committee of this Games decided on supplementary regulations that athletes who pre-select to compete across provinces will have their qualification for this Games cancelled. Therefore, the first to protest was Wu Bixian's qualification, and then protests continued to arise. It is not certain whether all those who protested this regulation in the Games competition regulations were based on sportsmanship, fair and upright. It is even possible that some were using it to settle scores or for revenge. In short, the law does not punish the past. The competition committee's regulations were well-intentioned, but the legislation was too late. If it is adopted in the next session, disputes can be avoided.

A Glimpse of the Traffic Situation During the National Games: The Number of Spectators and Cars is Astonishing, Setting a New Record in the History of Transportation in Our Country 189

The traffic group of the Games yesterday released a summary of the traffic situation during the Games, as follows:

Number of Spectators

During the National Games, there were five days when the number of participating spectators exceeded 100,000. The most was on National Day, with approximately 180,000 people. The second most was on October 18, with approximately 160,000 people. October 19 and 20 had no more than 150,000 people, and October 13 had only 100,000 people.

Traffic Order

During the National Games, the closing time was generally before 7:00 PM every day, except for Double Ten Day, when it suddenly rained at 4:00 PM in the afternoon, and spectators rushed to board the vehicles, causing the order to be slightly chaotic, and it was not completely cleared until 8:30 PM. For example, on October 19, although there were 150,000 spectators, the clearing was completed by 6:30 PM.

Car Count

Most of the spectators attending the National Games started arriving from 8:00 AM onwards, and many started returning to Shanghai after 3:00 PM during the three sessions. The number of vehicles traveling back and forth in one day was very large. However, due to the designated routes and other restrictions, it was not too crowded. On Double Ten Day alone, from 7:30 AM to 8:30 PM, there were approximately 12,000 vehicles traveling back and forth (detailed in the table below, empty vehicles not included). The situation on October 19 was slightly different. Because it was the football final and also a Saturday, most of the spectators went to the Games between 12:30 PM and 1:30 PM in the afternoon. During this one hour, there were 1,570 cars and 161 buses, a total of 1,731 vehicles (empty vehicles not included). When leaving, they all gathered between 5:00 PM and 9:30 PM, and were willing to leave only after the football final was completely over. Therefore, within this half hour, there were 1,460 cars and 210 buses passing through Xiangyin Road, a total of 1,670 vehicles. This can be said to be the highest record in transportation in our country.

Remaining Vehicles

As for the various vehicles used by the spectators, the number of people traveling by car was the largest, followed by buses, and then trains. For example, on Double Ten Day, there were more than 70,000 people traveling by car, approximately 60,000 people by bus (including those using cars), and approximately 10,000 people by train. Because it was National Day, all factories were closed for the day, so there were many workers participating. However, most of them walked to the meeting, and the number of pedestrians increased due to the sudden rain at 4:00 PM in the afternoon. It is estimated that the number of pedestrians on this day accounted for more than 50% of all spectators. As for other days, there were very few pedestrians. On October 19, the number of pedestrians was only about 5%.

The attendees included Zhang Deshan, Zou Guozhu, Zhang Dingzhi, Chen Xianda, Mou Hetian, Zhao Lianji, Zhong Wanshi, Zhou Wenlin, Zhang Shengshou, Jigu Kui, Li Hongzhang, Tan Mingyi, Song Jilian, Zhang Quanshan, Wadefu, Yang Wenjiong, Chen Xueren, Chen Sanguang, Zhang Qiquan, Zhang Yongshun, etc. After Zhang Deshan reported on the resolutions, the following was discussed: (1) Elect Zhang Deshan, Zou Guozhu, Mou Hetian, Zhang Dingzhi, and Chen Xianda as members of the preparatory committee, and elect Zhang Deshan as the director; (2) Invite Chairman Ma Lin, Major General Ma Bufang, Director Yang Xiyao, Director Tan Wikemin, Director Wei Fuzi, Director Li Naifen, Committee Member Wang Yingyu, Principal Qi Zhongdao, Dean Cao Wenhuan, Dean Ma Shirong, Chief Zhao Xianhou, Principal Wang Shoujun, Principal Wu Shijin, Principal Ma Xiaoshi, Principal Ma Shaowu, Director Kang Guanru, Director Wang Zhengang, Secretary Zhao Jitian, Special Commissioner Li Tianmin, Special Commissioner Yan Huatang, etc. as sponsors; (3) The preparatory director will discuss with the preparatory committee to handle all preparatory procedures. Qinghai has never had an organization for sports before. After the establishment of this association, it will be able to greatly promote sports in Qinghai in the future, and the prospects are promising.

Free Talk

On Hunger 196

— Cao Juren

A few days ago, Changjiang, a traveling correspondent for Ta Kung Pao, wrote a travelogue about Chengdu and Lanzhou. One section recorded the death of a starving person, saying:

"South of Hongqiaoguan, there was a dying man lying on the side of the road, his legs bent, his lips moving from time to time. The reporter gave him a steamed bun. His hands had lost consciousness, and his eyes could not open or close freely. He repeatedly touched his hand and placed the steamed bun between his lips and nose. After a long time, he moved his hand to take the steamed bun, and after a long time, he put the steamed bun in his mouth. After he took a bite, his whole body suddenly trembled, his mouth and eyes opened wide, and he stared straight at the reporters, making a 'woo woo' sound. Only those who have personally experienced hunger can know the taste of it."

Written in such a light-hearted way, it rushed straight to our hearts like a cold current. In the past, Emperor Hui of Jin made a joke that has been passed down through the ages, asking why the starving people didn't eat meat. Emperor Guangxu fled to Xi'an during the Boxer Rebellion in 1900, and he didn't eat for a long time on the way. He didn't know what was wrong, he just felt a stomach ache, which was the same joke. The taste of hunger cannot be known unless one has personally experienced it. The Norwegian writer Hamsun (Hamsun Knut 1860-) once wrote a novel with the theme of hunger—Hunger (written in 1888). Some sections can be compared with that correspondence:

"...Whenever I have endured any prolonged period of hunger, my brain seems to quietly escape from my skull, leaving me only an empty shell! My head gradually floats up, I cannot feel its weight on my shoulders, and when I look at anything, I actually open my eyes too wide." P.25

"...I walked lazily down the street, and at a place on Heigihajin Street, I stopped in front of a food store. There were many foods displayed in the store's window. A cat was lying there, sleeping soundly next to a round French loaf. Behind it were also a plate of lard and several plates of meat. I stood there for a while, staring at these foods, but remembering that I had no money to buy them, I suddenly turned my head and continued my wandering. ...A great confusion suddenly arose in my brain. I still staggered forward, determined not to pay attention to the confusion in my brain; but the more I walked, the worse I became, and finally I had to sit down on a step. My whole life changed. Something slipped inside me, and it seemed as if my brain net or brain face had been torn into two pieces." P.64

Complementing this state of hunger is a passage describing his gluttony after hunger, saying:

"I began to eat, eating more and more gluttonously, swallowing chunks of meat without chewing, eating each mouthful like a wild beast, and tearing the meat like a man-eating monster. ...After finishing, I immediately walked to the door; I already felt nauseous. The food began to act strangely, and I felt very uncomfortable, unable to bear it for even a moment. I had to vomit in every dark corner I passed. I struggled to suppress this nausea that would soon make me empty-bellied again; I clenched my hands, wanting to conquer it; I stomped my feet on the sidewalk, and I swallowed everything that came up. Everything was ineffective, and I finally jumped into a doorway, bent over, head forward, and the tears that burst out of my eyes blurred my eyes, and I vomited greatly. I was in terrible pain, sobbing and walking down the street." P.166

Hamsun writes very realistically about the physical changes of hunger. In the initial stage of hunger, it starts with the stomach, as if something is pricking in the gastrointestinal area, which is what Emperor Guangxu called a stomach ache. Furthermore, the symptoms of brain swelling and nausea occur together. When the head shakes, the eyes are full of stars. After about three to five days of hunger, in the third stage of hunger, the head is light and the feet are weak, the limbs are weak, and like a patient, one breathes constantly. Generally speaking, hunger is very painful. Hong Chengchou, a minister of the Ming Dynasty who was captured by the Qing army, prepared to starve to death to show his patriotism. After a few days of starvation, he could not support it anymore. A cup of rice juice was poured down, which induced his desire to live, and he continued to live and became a surrendered minister of the Manchu Qing. (Before Master Hongyi entered the mountains to practice, he meditated and starved for two weeks: according to him, his heart was calm and very comfortable, which can only be considered an exception.)

The psychological changes in hunger are much more complex than the physical changes. Hamsun said that when a person is hungry for a long time, he sees every passerby as an enemy, even if they are wearing a single shirt, he sees them as arrogant. This means that hunger arouses hatred. During the great famine in Shanxi during the Guangxu period, there was a news report that a person from another province was slaughtered and eaten by the victims. From hatred to cannibalism is also a reasonable thing to do. The early sages of Confucianism also acknowledged that ordinary people are prone to reckless behavior when they are hungry, and also acknowledged the tragic situation of people eating each other.

But they believed that a cultivated gentleman should show different integrity in hunger. The Book of Rites, Tan Gong, records a Qi man who fainted from hunger. Qian Ao greeted him with a compassionate tone, but he stubbornly refused to eat the "food thrown in contempt" and eventually starved to death. Although Zengzi did not approve of the Qi man's eventual starvation to death, he very much approved of the Qi man's stubborn refusal of the compassionate tone.

We have never seen a Confucian gentleman. The legend of Boyi and Shuqi starving to death on Shouyang Mountain is not very credible. After the Three Dynasties, we only saw an hungry poet Tao Yuanming, who was somewhat close to the Confucian ideal. After Tao Yuanming returned to the fields, his situation was generally not very good. Once, Tan Daoji, the governor of Jiangzhou, went to visit him. He had been lying in bed for several days with a hungry stomach. Tan Daoji personally comforted him and gave him meat and millet; he waved his hand to refuse, simply not appreciating it. He fully practiced the Confucian proposition in this way. He also has a poem of begging for food, describing how he begged for food from his neighbors when he had no food to eat. The neighbors knew that he was poor and often kept him for meals. The poem ends with the four words "I am grateful for your kindness, but ashamed of my lack of talent. How can I repay you? I will repay you in the dark," expressing how deeply engraved in his heart was his gratitude for the neighbors' hospitality! When people are poor, they easily become very sensitive, and causeless anger and excessive gratitude often accompany each other. We believe that Han Xin's "a meal's kindness will never be forgotten" and Hamsun's "seeing every passerby as an enemy" can coexist.

Literature is a feeling of real life; Mr. Lu Xun said; "As for the experience of life, not to mention anything else; as for the matter of being hungry, if you like it, you can try it. As long as you don't eat for two days, the aroma of rice will create a special temptation." It seems too early for those who do not have this minimum experience of life of "being hungry" to write about literature, although "being hungry" is not elegant or "leisurely".

Morning 197

— Floating Ice

The autumn of an island nation perhaps arrives extraordinarily early. A letter from a friend in my homeland still says: "The weather in Shanghai remains the same, and the swimming pools are still open." Yet the mornings in Tokyo already bring a chilling air.

Having come to this island nation, a month has already slipped by in a flash. I love the mornings in a foreign land the most, those tranquil mornings carrying a cool air. Every morning, I must walk alone on the deserted dirt roads, my feet stepping on tall "geta" sandals, so that even if it's muddy, my heels won't get stained. Above is a hazy sky, without a single cloud, not even a lark. The desolate sky is more desolate than my desolate mood. Sometimes, there might be a blurred white mist, using a faint atmosphere to congeal the earth. However, what a powerless gas it is!

I tread upon this quiet morning, gazing at everything around me. The dense houses, the wooden buildings, are still sleeping. Only the chimney of the bathhouse, which had been belching flames all night, still strains its tired body, stretching its arms in mid-air. Occasionally, one or two barks of a dog break the long silence, but even this rarely disturbs my peaceful mood.

At this time, past life floats up in my silent heart, like a lone boat in the ocean. That year of life was a dream, a nightmare. Around me, surrounded by many seductive poisonous claws, sensual tones, life had long robbed me of the courage to fight. I immersed myself in the turbid torrent, like duckweed, drifting with the waves, as if a lone boat in the ocean encountered a tremendous hurricane, with mountain-like waves surging fiercely around me. At times, I also wanted to struggle. I cried out angrily, but this cry only fueled the mocking laughter of the raging waves. My surroundings were then filled with an extremely dense black atmosphere. I couldn't see the sunlight, let alone the red light of a star.

However, I still had a last breath of strength. I uttered a primal cry from the depths of my heart, reminding me of the strength of my ancestors, reminding me of my past spirit. "You're still young! A young man of twenty!" A loud, resounding voice warned me in my heart. So, I opened my dull eyes, stretched out my arms, and let out a long howl in the black ocean. It was the battle cry of charging in a primal struggle. I picked up the oar again and fought against the dark, raging waves. Finally, I broke through the deep, black atmosphere and saw the red light on the opposite shore.

At that moment, light shone from all sides. I met my former brothers again. "Comrades, I'm back!" I shouted joyfully, regardless of whether they heard me, regardless of whether they still cast doubtful glances at me. However, I had triumphed from the struggle. I celebrated myself in this quiet, cool morning light.

Reflecting on this past struggle, my lonely heart surged with fervor. The blood throughout my body circulated. Suddenly, a long howl echoed in mid-air. The city began to roar. I looked up and saw a bright rising sun in the east!

I will tread upon this cool morning light, counting the surging pulses of my blood.

Honorary Old Woman (11) 198

— Jiang Ma Xiu, Translated by Ren Jun

"Hey, I am Yongzao's substitute!" The old woman's eyes sparkled; Number One walked around in the narrow room, waving her hands, and said in an extremely agitated tone: "I am a corporal, rank six, a glorious war death. Hey, let's all drink happily, drink until we collapse! I have simply never been happier. Glory, glory! Ah, this is glory, this is glory!"

Then, the old woman danced with strange hand and foot movements, elated.

From this point on, people were convinced that the old woman had truly gone mad.

After the funeral, the cooking old woman came to my house early in the morning, as usual, and worked until night. She worked as well as ever, without any signs of madness. The only difference was that her speech contained more laughable elements and she took out the "cat skin" and plucked it in the dormitory more frequently than before. Although the people at home sympathized with her, they also found it quite difficult to deal with.

Another very obvious thing was the excessive use of the two words "honor." The nickname "Honorary Old Woman" started from this time.

Once, I was in a hurry to go to the factory because of something. At that time, I tripped over something and fell.

"This is honor, this is honor, get up quickly!"

The old woman shouted this in the worker's dormitory.

I got up. My knees were badly scraped, bleeding a lot.

"It doesn't matter!" The old woman said more seriously when she saw this situation: "Glorious wounds, a medal is coming."

These things were nothing. At that time, it was, without a doubt, a common catchphrase. However, the old woman loved cats very much; she often picked them up, kissing their cheeks as if she liked them very much, and said to them:

"Lovely cat, honorary cat!"

In the same tone, she continued to use "honorary flower," "honorary brother," "honorary wife," and so on.

One day, near the old woman's house, a poor, single old man hanged himself. She ran to my mother and described the old man's kindness and his poor and lonely life with deep sympathy; then, with tears in her eyes, she said:

"I think this is so pitiful! But this is also honor!"

My mother laughed.

"There is no honor in a person hanging themselves."

"It is also honor." The old woman stubbornly insisted on her own opinion very seriously. "Although he didn't die in battle; but, he died in destitution. I think this is also honor..."

"Then," my mother laughed even harder, "like your son, the government will probably issue about three hundred taels to this hanged old man."

"Probably so. It is truly a glorious thing."

The old woman said seriously all along.

My mother found it very funny. Then, my mother explained to her in detail how death in battle and death by hanging are different, and what honor really means. However, the old woman did not listen to my mother at all. She just said:

"Honor! An enviable thing!"

Around Lunchtime 199

— Lin Shi

Before ten o'clock, I was urging my wife to quickly cook lunch, because I had arranged to go to Mr. Qin's house at noon. Mr. Qin had recently become an official, and I was confident that future interactions with him would be of no small help to me. Of course, I am not someone without self-awareness. I am not fit to be an official, and I do not want to be one, but to introduce me to a small job to relieve my poverty would not be too difficult for him, I thought.

In any case, I have been unemployed for too long, from September of the year before last until now. For these full two years, I have been relying on publishing some articles piecemeal, fortunately, my family has not starved to death. But now it is very different. Bookstores do not have the resources to buy manuscripts and publish single volumes, and the lively magazines of the year have also successively ceased publication, so even if I write non-stop every day, I cannot exchange it for money.

Yes, I have been writing non-stop for two years, writing non-stop, even if I cannot write, I have to write, which has caused me to feel great pain. Of course, this is for the sake of my family's livelihood. But apart from this, there is also the reason for writing; to embellish my life with writing is my most important career, like the lark's cry high in the clouds, which is its own need for life, and also to make the world more beautiful. However, this is an inappropriate metaphor; can I freely soar in the sky? And is the world made more beautiful by the cry of this little lark? On the contrary, I am only fit to be a cuckoo, crying day and night, even if the crying is mixed with a heavy bloody smell, telling people that the world is infinitely desolate, which is also my duty! Otherwise, I can only be a sparrow shivering in front of the eaves in winter. When white snow tightly covers the earth, not allowing me to find any food to feed myself and the hungry children in the nest, I have to chirp, although this low cry may not get a drop of sympathy from the empty world, I still struggle to live on!

This is my last courage; in any case, I must struggle to live on. The small grass that grows in the arid desert is also the goodwill of nature's creation, who can suppress its right to grow? Unfortunately, I was born with a stubborn personality, and unfortunately, my ancestors and father bequeathed me shame and justice, which makes me unfit to live in this cruel era. Ah! This cruel era! How many young people have been driven to the line of death amidst national ruin, family destruction, natural disasters, and wars, and how many young people are unemployed, enduring hunger.

These things, these things, I have been repeatedly thinking about recently, and I am thinking about them again today.

After eating, I put on my clothes, took the two dimes my wife gave me for the bus fare, and walked out the door with great hope. On the road, I saw that my black leather shoes were very shiny, which was my wife's careful love for me. Because of this, I immediately remembered my wife's words:

"You are bitten in the heart by poverty, you are too decadent. You have to cheer up, don't forget to pile up a smile on your face, when you ask your friends to find you a job, don't make people look down on my husband!"

Yes, this sentence is very correct, why should I be laughed at because of poverty? At least I should not forget that I am also a person, I cannot be despised and insulted because of poverty. So I straightened my chest and made the leather shoes walk loudly on the road. I touched my newly shaved beard and my hair, which I had applied a lot of Vaseline to in the morning, and I pretended to be very satisfied with my good luck.

The road to Mr. Qin's house is not very far, with my vigorous spirit, I can walk there in less than half an hour. So I saved the streetcar fare, and it would be good to leave it to buy vegetables tomorrow. If the opportunity is good, if Mr. Qin is willing to take care of me and give me a position, then it would be more comfortable and glorious to come back by rickshaw immediately, wouldn't it? Thinking of this, I couldn't restrain the joy in my heart. A few days ago, I had left a note at his house, stating that I would go to his house to talk to him at twelve o'clock today when he came home for lunch. Although the note did not specify what to talk about, but with my three years of old friendship with him, and his clear knowledge of my unemployment, how could he not understand my intention?

No matter from which aspect, Mr. Qin is truly my good friend who understands me. After I lost my job, he lent me a large sum of money when he had not yet become an official; I have not yet repaid it until now, and I feel a little sorry in my heart. But as long as I have a job, I will first repay his loan, although he may not be waiting for this money to use.

Soon, I walked to the gate of Mr. Qin's house, which had a parakeet hanging on it. I pressed the doorbell, walked into the living room, and stepped on the soft carpet. But he had not yet returned. Mrs. Qin cordially invited me to sit on the velvet sofa. He had recently rented this new-style foreign house, and the decorations on the walls and the furnishings in the house were very elegant. I casually flipped through the pictorial on the table, patiently waiting for him to return.

After about twenty minutes, Mr. Qin called; because he had to attend a banquet, he would not come home for lunch. This immediately made me feel worried. Afterwards, Mrs. Qin let me talk to him on the phone, and I said:

"Mr. Qin, aren't you coming back? I am waiting for you."

"Hello!" His voice was still so bright. "Because there is something going on, I can't come back. What do you want to talk to me about?"

"It's nothing, just chatting casually." I was shy, how could I say it directly? In the end, I boldly told him, and he said:

"Have you looked for others to help you find a way?"

"I have looked for many people, but no one can help..."

"But I can't help either!" His voice was very loud; "Okay, let's talk about it later."

I walked out of the gate of his house dejectedly, the parakeet on the frame seemed to give me a bitter smile. I felt very tired, but I still walked home. In any case, I still have to live on, and it is always enough to leave two dimes to buy vegetables tomorrow.

Record of Leg Amputation (Part 1) 201

— Yue Qi

The first application of the "persuasion" story

——Medical Story Eleven——

October 16, 1846, is a great day worth commemorating. If you don't believe it, read the story recorded by Dr. G. M. Angell below.

The story took place at the Massachusetts General Hospital in Boston. This is a hospital founded in 1811 with a long history in the United States. At that time, the chief surgeon was Dr. John Warren, who also served as a professor of surgery at Harvard University.

In the winter of 1846, medical students in Boston heard a message: Someone had invented an anesthetic that could eliminate the pain of patients undergoing surgery. Later, they heard another message: Dr. Warren of Massachusetts General Hospital would use this anesthetic when amputating a patient's leg. This message soon spread to newspapers throughout the city, causing discussion in the medical community. Before that time, several anesthetics had been tested, but some were only suitable for tooth extraction, and some completely failed. Until then, a completely applicable anesthetic for major surgery had not actually been invented. This message aroused great interest, as expected.

"On the morning of October 16," Dr. Angell said, "I ran to the hospital as usual, but much earlier than usual, because judging from Dr. Warren's reputation and the importance of this experiment, I determined that there would be many people attending.

"When I arrived, the hospital gate was already crowded with a large group of people, the end of the line extending to the street. The gate was still closed and would not open until a certain time. I led a student through the side door and ran straight into the operating room, selected a seat, and sat there waiting. The layout of the operating room was like a circular theater, with several rows of seats arranged on three sides. The seats were surrounded by railings, inside the railings was an operating table, and behind it was a door leading to the hospital ward.

"The seats of me and my companion were in the front row, directly opposite the operating table. At this time, the crowd outside the door gathered more and more; when the gate opened, they poured into the circular theater like a tide, packed tightly, and many could not find a seat, so they had to stand and wait.

"Soon, Dr. Warren walked in, followed by a young man. The young man held a glass ball in his hand, about eight inches in diameter, with a mouth at the top, plugged with a wooden gun, and filled with a transparent liquid; we did not know what it was.

I personally did not know this young man; I only knew from the whispers of the person next to me that he was Dr. Morton, the inventor of the new anesthetic to be tested this time.

"After a while, the attendant brought the patient to be operated on and placed them on the operating table. The patient was a woman, about twenty-four or five years old. Three young interns stood side by side opposite Dr. Warren, and Dr. Morton stood by the railing, no more than a few feet from our seats, holding the glass ball filled with transparent liquid in his hand."

Dr. Warren began to discuss the condition. He explained that the patient was suffering from ischial osteomyelitis of the knee joint. He stated that various methods of alleviating pain had been used on the patient, but none had been effective. Therefore, the patient had to have their leg amputated. He had explained this to the patient, informing them that there was no other way, and had obtained the patient's consent.

When Dr. Warren said this, the entire audience was silent. From the front row to the back row, not a single whisper was heard, nor the sound of writing with a pencil.

Dr. Warren slowly turned his head, faced the audience, and said in a particularly solemn tone:

Things to Know About Quitting Opium (2) 202

— Zhang Zhongming

Chapter 2: The Value of Opium in Medicine

Opium does indeed occupy an important position in pharmacology. Its effectiveness is rapid and its treatment is miraculously effective. Other drugs often lament their inferiority. When used properly, patients are amazed by its miraculousness. Otherwise, many abuses arise, which are unimaginable. Discussing the effects of opium, a small amount is stimulating, a large amount is anesthetic, and more than that causes acute poisoning. Regular use leads to chronic poisoning, which is the various phenomena described in the previous chapter after smoking.

Physicians should be cautious and thorough in the application of opium. Even a slight negligence can easily lead to poisoning. Special attention should be paid to children taking it. According to reports, children often die from dysentery caused by using opium ash. This is all due to ignorance of the pharmacology of opium. As for the value of opium in medicine, it is only a good medicine for treating symptoms and saving lives. Judging from its fundamental therapeutic efficacy, it is very limited. Hearing this suddenly, one may suspect it is inaccurate, but once one examines the reality, it is rarely difficult to understand. For example, to treat cough, we can use opium to suppress it, but fundamental treatment requires expectorants. Another example is abdominal pain, which can also be treated with opium, but to prevent its recurrence, one must use methods to clear the intestines. From this point of view, the effect of opium can only be a supplementary agent for fundamental treatment and cannot be used as the sole main medicine. If one does the opposite and uses opium exclusively to treat diseases, the result will inevitably be the pain of addiction developing and the disease not being cured. Those who use opium to treat diseases should think deeply about this. Opium is not a good medicine for fundamental treatment, but its emergency rescue and symptom-treating effects have indelible achievements in medicine. When acute diseases occur (such as severe pain), anesthetic drugs must be used to relieve the crisis momentarily. Otherwise, the patient will be moaning in pain and unable to undergo any examination or treatment.

Moreover, opium is highly addictive, so its use should only be limited to a short period. If taken for a slightly longer period, it will develop into chronic poisoning, which is no different from smoking opium. Once chronic poisoning develops, its effects gradually diminish. Initially, a large amount can still achieve a momentary effect, but as the opium addiction deepens, even strong drugs are not easily effective. Therefore, doctors have no good solution when those with deep addiction need emergency treatment. This is why. Now, the effects of opium are listed as follows:

(1) Pain: All kinds of pain after major and minor surgeries, as well as stomach pain, abdominal pain, etc., are easily suppressed. However, it is ineffective for headaches.

(2) Diarrhea: Opium has the effect of stopping gastrointestinal motility, so it can be used as an antidiarrheal agent.

(3) Asthma and cough: Opium has the effect of calming qi and stopping cough.

(4) Insomnia: Most effective for insomnia caused by pain.

(5) Nerve stimulation: Has miraculous effects on brain stimulation, such as epilepsy, brain spasm, and poisoning.

(6) Internal bleeding: Such as lung bleeding and gastrointestinal bleeding. Because opium has the effect of reducing internal organ movement, it is often used in the medical field as a hemostatic adjuvant.

Chapter 3: Methods of Quitting Opium

There are many methods of quitting opium, and most of them are effective. Sometimes, even immortal water talismans and incantations can lead to abstinence. Sometimes, even truly scientific methods fail. There is no other reason. Opium is a nerve toxin. The psychology of smokers is most easily unpredictable. They often abandon their great efforts due to extremely small setbacks, or doubt and fear the diseases after quitting, are indecisive, or yearn for the pleasure of smoking and have no determination to quit. This kind of psychology not only hesitates when about to quit but often occurs after quitting. Therefore, doctors must first understand the psychology of smokers and constantly encourage their courage to make the determination to quit. Those undergoing abstinence should also accept the doctor's guidance with complete faith. Then the progress of quitting opium will be twice the result with half the effort.

Whether quitting opium is painful is one of the most concerning issues for smokers. But when asking them one by one, they are often troubled by the environment and cannot speak frankly and directly. Why? If one speaks of its advantages (such as reporting that there is no pain at all, working as usual, being full of energy, etc.), then the occurrence of pain in the future will inevitably leave a basis for deceiving and exaggerating. If one speaks of its disadvantages (such as various uncomfortable phenomena after quitting), it will increase the smokers' doubts and fears, making them dare not attempt to quit opium. However, in reality, there will inevitably be discomfort during the abstinence period. This is undeniably true. If one can endure it for a while, there will eventually be a day when bitterness ends and sweetness comes. Those quitting should deeply understand this.

Common Sense about Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene 203

— Tang Renji

(68) Stomatitis (Continued)

(Second) Ulcerative Stomatitis

The causes of ulcerative stomatitis are mostly infection and poisoning. It easily occurs in crowded places such as barracks, prisons, and orphanages when infectious. When caused by poisoning, it is mostly due to taking mercury-containing drugs internally. This condition is specifically called mercurial stomatitis, which is frequently encountered clinically. Poisoning from lead, phosphorus, arsenic, and copper is less common. Patients with anemia, weakness, tuberculosis, diabetes, scurvy, glandular disease, and rickets are also prone to this disease.

The main symptom of this disease is necrosis that first occurs in the gingival mucosa of the lower jaw, gradually spreading to the oral mucosa of the lips and cheeks. This change in the gums is most evident in severe mercurial stomatitis. When ulcers occur, they are usually covered with purulent matter. The gums are red and swollen and bleed easily. Once necrosis and ulceration occur in the gingival margin mucosa, the teeth often become loose and may even fall out. Saliva secretion is particularly vigorous. Lymph nodes in the jaw, neck, etc., are often swollen, and the mouth develops a foul odor. Patients usually feel pain in the mouth, making eating difficult. The course of the disease is about eight to fourteen days. Its treatment is roughly the same as that for catarrhal stomatitis.

(Third) Aphthous Stomatitis

Aphthous stomatitis is often epidemic. Weak children are most likely to develop it. Its main cause is mostly poor oral hygiene and irritation of the oral mucosa by sharp teeth during the first teething period in children. In addition, it often occurs during the course of infectious diseases such as pneumonia, typhoid fever, measles, and scarlet fever, as well as during menstruation, postpartum, and lactation in women.

The main symptom of this disease is the appearance of yellow or grayish-white spots on the oral mucosa, about the size of a pinhead or a small bean, slightly raised, with a deep red halo around them. These spots occur most often on the edge of the tongue and frenulum, and less often on the lips and buccal mucosa. The spots are generally firmly attached to the mucosal surface, making them very difficult to peel off. If forced, they will bleed. Patients usually feel burning, dryness, pain, and increased saliva secretion in the mouth. Eating is naturally difficult. In addition, it is noteworthy that children often develop high fever. The course of the disease is about one or two weeks, but it is prone to recurrence. The treatment strategy is also to clean the mouth, avoid irritation, and frequently rinse with mouthwash (or wash the mouth in children).

Common Sense Q&A About Teeth (6) 204

— Lin Jianxian

(Question 26) How many more permanent teeth are there than primary teeth?

(Answer) Everything else is the same, except that there are three more molars on each side than primary teeth, for a total of twelve more teeth.

(Question 27) Many middle-aged people do not have thirty-two teeth, but are missing one or two, or two or three. What is the reason?

(Answer) This is because the third molar on the inside has not yet grown out. This tooth is often buried under the gums in the jawbone. Sometimes it doesn't come out until the age of thirty or forty. This tooth will be discussed later.

(Question 28) Do each of the permanent teeth have their own specific functions?

(Answer) Generally speaking, incisors are used to bite and cut food, so they are shaped like chisels; canines are used to tear food, so they are shaped like cones; molars are used to crush and grind food, so their occlusal surface is large and has raised and sunken patterns like a millstone. In terms of chewing function, molars are the most important. Therefore, molars should be carefully protected and not allowed to decay.

(Question 29) Which molar is the most important?

(Answer) It is the first molar. There is one on each side of the jaw, top and bottom. It can be considered the cornerstone of the dental arch. If it decays and falls out, the other permanent teeth are easily loosened, leading to tilting and decay. Moreover, chewing becomes difficult. In addition, the chin will recede, and the face will become asymmetrical. Therefore, this molar should not be allowed to decay and be lost. Parents should not mistakenly think that it is a temporary primary tooth and not pay attention to it.

(Question 30) How can the first molar not be mistaken for a primary tooth?

(Answer) (1) It comes out only at the age of six (so it is commonly called the six-year molar). (2) It grows next to the back primary molar, on the inside. If a child has three molars in their mouth, the one on the innermost side (the sixth one counting from the central incisor) is undoubtedly it. (3) It is whiter and larger than the primary molars. From these three points, it can be distinguished from a primary tooth.

(Question 31) If a permanent tooth decays and is lost, or is extracted, will another tooth grow out to replace it?

(Answer) Once a permanent tooth is lost, no tooth will ever grow back. Therefore, permanent teeth should be treasured.

Chapter 3 The Structure and Parts of Teeth

(Question 32) How are teeth formed?

(Answer) Teeth can be said to grow from epidermal cells, just like fingernails and hair. The mucous membrane in our mouth is a layer of epidermis. Inside it, there are odontoblasts. Initially, it is soft tissue, which gradually calcifies and becomes hard bone tissue, thus forming teeth.

(Question 33) How many segments can a tooth be divided into from head to toe?

(Answer) It can be divided into three segments: (1) The crown, which accounts for about one-third of the total length, is the part exposed outside the gums. (2) The neck, which is at the edge of the gums. (3) The root, which is embedded in the alveolar socket.

(Question 34) How many roots does a tooth have?

(Answer) Incisors, canines, and premolars all have only one root (sometimes the upper premolars have two roots). Lower molars have two roots. Upper molars have three roots. But there are many exceptions.

(Question 35) How many layers can a tooth be divided into?

(Answer) It can be divided into three layers, the main parts: the outermost layer is enamel. The second layer is dentin. The innermost layer is pulp.

Medical Science of Pain Relief (37) 205

— Li Xing

This type of medicine can be used, but it is important to note that the first priority in pain relief should be to remove the cause of the pain. Once the cause is removed and the pain stops, it will not recur. If one does not seek to remove the cause but only seeks to relieve the pain, it is actually equivalent to ladling boiling water. Therefore, it is in line with medical science to treat the cause of the disease while taking a certain amount of pain medication when in pain. Note that sometimes using other beneficial and harmless therapies, such as heat therapy, hydrotherapy, and diathermy, is better than taking pain medication. Taking pain medication should be used as a temporary or very short-term emergency measure: for example, if a headache occurs in the middle of the night, one can take pain medication, but the next day one should seek fundamental treatment for the headache, and should not just take pain medication every time one has a headache. Pain medication will not cure the disease, it only temporarily suppresses the sensation of pain. Furthermore, although pain medication is not particularly harmful to the body when used infrequently, it is also not beneficial. Long-term internal use is harmful to the body. Therefore, using pain medication is a symptomatic treatment, not a root treatment. By using pain medication according to these principles, one can obtain benefits, but if one takes pain medication haphazardly, the result will inevitably be half benefit and half harm. I will briefly describe the types of pain medication below:

Salicylate Compounds

The most important drugs in this class are: (1) sodium salicylate, (2) acetylsalicylic acid (i.e., aspirin), (3) methyl salicylate (i.e., wintergreen oil), and (4) cinchophen. Generally speaking, these drugs, in addition to their pain-relieving effect, do not have any particular toxicity if not taken in excessive amounts. These drugs also have antipyretic effects. These drugs are mostly used for rheumatic diseases and neuralgia, acute arthritis, etc. These drugs do not appear to have any particular effect on other chronic painful conditions.

Sodium Salicylate is mostly used for acute arthritis and rheumatic pain, and it is very effective when used properly. Note that for rheumatic pain caused by carditis, this drug can only temporarily relieve pain and reduce fever, but it will recur after stopping the drug, because the drug cannot cure carditis. Taking too much internally can cause symptoms such as nausea, vomiting, and tinnitus. These side effects will stop after stopping the drug. Taking too much internally can also suppress the nervous system, respiratory system, or suppress blood flow, leading to collapse, and sometimes miscarriage can occur. The usual dose starts from one gram. It is best taken with sodium bicarbonate.

Aspirin is the most famous pain reliever. It is quite effective for relieving headaches, neuralgia, rheumatic pain, etc. In addition to its pain-relieving effect, aspirin also has an antipyretic effect. Its pain-relieving effect is probably due to suppressing sensation, and its antipyretic effect is to reduce the body's metabolism and increase the body's heat dissipation. Each internal dose can last for several hours at most, after which it must be taken again. It is okay to use it for temporary pain relief, but it is unreasonable to take it for a long time. Using this drug can be said to be treating the symptoms, while treating the root cause requires finding the cause of the pain and then treating the symptoms accordingly. For example, it is a proper way to take it temporarily for a toothache or headache, but it is wrong to rely entirely on these drugs to treat every toothache or every headache, because only by understanding the cause and then removing the source of the disease can the pain be permanently eliminated. If the source of the disease is not removed, the pain may recur at any time. Then, taking these drugs internally for a long time without seeking to remove the cause of the disease is inevitably a pointless敷衍. For example, if the cause of the headache is syphilitic pain, it is also reasonable to take pain medication when the pain is extreme, but the fundamental treatment is to inject a special drug for syphilis.

Methyl Salicylate (Wintergreen Oil) has similar medicinal properties to sodium salicylate. Applying it externally to swollen and painful areas, such as arthritis and neuritis, also has a pain-relieving effect. Internal use can also relieve pain, but it is more toxic. For external application, one part of this drug mixed with two parts of olive oil is the appropriate amount. This drug does not need to be taken internally. If one ounce is taken internally at once, it can be life-threatening.

Cinchophen (also known as Atophan) has the same properties as sodium salicylate and aspirin and is also used to relieve pain. Neocinchophen is the same. Do not use too much of this drug, or for too long, as the side effects are very severe.

Brief Introduction to Pulmonary Tuberculosis (71) 206

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 12 Treatment of Pulmonary Tuberculosis

Section 3 Rest and Nutrition

Taking a step back, even if it is suitable for high-altitude convalescence, we must never be overly superstitious about the climate here, believing that it has an incredible effect on this disease. This view is completely wrong. Because there is absolutely no climate that is universally effective for all pulmonary tuberculosis patients; if such words are spread, it must be "Xiang Zhuang's sword dance," "the old drunkard's intention is not in the wine," we should recognize this clearly. The doctor's purpose in advising the patient to change location is not only to rely on the climate of the new location, but to enable the patient to correctly implement the principles of health convalescence. What must not be forgotten is the rule of air therapy. Furthermore, once the patient leaves home, all the bad habits and environmental stimuli that usually hinder convalescence can be completely improved, which is greatly beneficial to the future of the disease. If one abandons these two and relies solely on the climate to seek good results, that will of course greatly disappoint the recipient.

So what is the true value of convalescence in a different location? It can be effective in early infiltration, proliferation, and sclerotic forms (even if expansive). It is particularly effective in reducing or eliminating fever and increasing appetite; all other symptoms can also be reduced as a result.

Of course, there are a very large number of patients who cannot afford to convalesce in a different location due to their personal financial situation, but they must not be pessimistic. If they pay sufficient attention in their own home or near their hometown, and strictly observe various convalescence rules, the results are not necessarily less than those of patients convalescing in a different location. Because, with the exception of all other things, there is a distinction between rich and poor, but nature treats everyone equally; the so-called fresh air is something that everyone can enjoy, and does not require material rewards! I respectfully offer this truth to the readers of this book!

Anti-Slave Girl Movement 207

— Chui

In the previous local supplement of Shen Bao, Mr. Meng Ruo published an article "Anti-Slave Girl Movement," which was very pleasant to read, but after thinking about it carefully, these are all grand words spoken in a hall, not heartfelt conversations in an inner room. Chinese people like to "speak official language," and this is one of those cases. Here, I would like to raise two questions about the practice of keeping slave girls:

First, which parents would not cherish their daughters and willingly sell them to others as slave girls?

Second, are all slave girls abused by their masters, like a certain young lady in Tianjin?

Assuming the answer is no, I have a few words to say. Impoverished couples cannot afford to eat their fill, but their sexual urges cannot be ignored, so they commit a great wrong and produce such an abomination. Do they kill it? They can't bear to. Do they raise it? They can't afford to. As a last resort, they sell this piece of their heart. This can both feed their daughter and feed themselves, and the system of keeping slave girls is born from this.

As for people keeping slave girls, there is also a reason for it. Originally, they wanted to hire servants, but even if they hired servants, if they could buy slave girls, they could have someone to order around and save someone in need, which is a double benefit. It does not necessarily mean that they are irritable and have nowhere to vent, so they buy a slave girl to abuse in every way, beat her severely, and scold her to vent the anger in their belly. If that were the case, why would I allow others to buy slave girls, but Mr. Meng Ruo cannot keep slave girls? Because he wants to use slave girls to vent his anger.

Although I have heard of cases of abusing slave girls, such masters are all tyrannical by nature, like the madam in a brothel or a certain young lady in Tianjin. Otherwise, there are tens of thousands of families keeping slave girls, and the number of abuse cases is relatively small. One cannot say that because an incest case occurred in a certain province, most people in that province are parricides. One cannot say that because a case of murdering one's husband occurred in a certain place, most women in that place are murderers of their husbands. Such reasoning is inappropriate. Therefore, although a certain young lady in Tianjin abused slave girls, it cannot be said that most slave owners are like a certain young lady in Tianjin. Furthermore, people who are tyrannical by nature will abuse not only slave girls but also servants, and not only servants but also in-laws and daughters-in-law. Assuming that there are cases of abusing servants and abusing in-laws and daughters-in-law, does that mean that we should abolish the master-servant system and the in-law-daughter-in-law system altogether? I am afraid that is also impossible.

The term "slave girl system" is not appropriate in the first place. Keeping slave girls is only a custom, not a system. All so-called systems contain legal or compulsory elements. Although the government has no explicit prohibition against keeping slave girls, it also has no measures to encourage it. This is a kind of buying and selling behavior combined by folk customs and needs. If you call it a system, I would consider it an excellent system, as it can both save the poor and provide convenience.

Mr. Meng Ruo also said that in the passive aspect, one must start with rescuing slave girls. I think this is the active aspect, not the passive aspect. However, Mr. Meng Ruo's only way to rescue slave girls is to set up a slave girl rescue center to accommodate slave girls who are unwilling to be slave girls or who are abused. I am afraid this is still not enough, because to rescue slave girls, one must first save the parents of the slave girls, and then the system of keeping slave girls will naturally be abolished. But may I ask if the country's finances are like this, the local finances are like this, and the social phenomena are like this, is there a way to do it? In the local matchmaking industry, old women are so numerous that there is almost no place to stand. I think that if the system of keeping slave girls could be made public, the slave girl trading industry would also prosper in the same way. Therefore, I would like to ask Mr. Meng Ruo to first understand the social phenomena and then carry out the anti-slave girl movement.

Lonely Song 208

— Shixi

I feel so lonely, especially in every moment facing the lonely lamp and melancholy.

It seems like it was last year, I drifted out of the bloody palms of my hometown, exhausted and hungry, wandering: from this corner to another corner, and from another corner to this corner, like a camel covered in musk heading towards the desolate Siberian plain.

In ××, by chance, I met a long-lost friend. She was a cheerful person with a round face, a short stature, and a smile on her face, always squinting her eyes. She always faced things optimistically. She was a determinist who believed that there was nothing imperfect in the world; but that meeting quickly exposed the shaking of her subjective views. She began to learn to frown, smile wryly, and worry.

On a dark road, accompanied by our thin shadows, we walked lightly. She coughed softly, raised her head to look at the indifferent lamplight for a moment, then smiled coldly, and said to me sadly:

"Friend! You have really changed, you have become so melancholy, quiet..."

I still lowered my head and strode forward silently, the hobnails of my leather shoes knocking on the cement with a rhythmic, light and bright sound. The sound seemed so gloomy and desolate on this gray and quiet street!…

A breeze blew across the sea, carrying dampness and cold.

She shivered slightly, and then yawned a few loud yawns in annoyance. After a long silence, her long, annoyed tone vibrated in the silence again.

"In the past few years, I have also changed because of the hardships of life. Really, sometimes I not only feel that I am so melancholy, but also lonely..." Then there was a long sigh.

"Someone said: Loneliness is like an invisible termite in the human body, gnawing at the hearts of every young person with the fluctuations of life..." She had just said this when she began to sob again, shaking her head sadly.

A melancholy and lonely song came from the fishing boat on the sea, the tone carrying terrible melancholy and desolation.

My thoughts began to be a little confused, and I murmured in a low voice: "What time is it?..."

She quickly interjected: "Maybe it's about nine o'clock!"

"I should go back to the hotel!" I said silently, and stopped.

"What's the hurry?" she shouted anxiously.

We walked in silence like this for several minutes, when she suddenly seemed to remember something important and asked me in a low voice, "Sometimes you feel lonely, my good friend, do you ever think of suicide?" She cast a probing look at me solemnly.

"No!" I shook my head and continued, "I only long to sing lonely songs!"

A song was sobbing from the seaside again, she raised her head in emotion and looked blankly at the wide sky, and after a long time, she sighed in a low voice: "That's it! The lonely song?" Tears fell down in a rustling sound.

The next day I left ××, and since then we have not had the opportunity to meet again. When I arrived in Shanghai, I also received a pair of short and enthusiastic letters from her, she said: "Friend! You are right, loneliness is terrible; but I have also begun to learn to sing that - lonely song!…"

I didn't reply to her letter, and I didn't receive any more letters from her. Later, I received news from another friend that she had been arrested.

Lonely people grow old and die in the lonely songs; however, I am still advancing with it in this desolate wilderness of life.

The Feeling of Smoke 209

— Whispers

When the state of mind falls into complete emptiness, the heart becomes as cold and empty as a vacuum. At this time, the world seems to be completely destroyed, and oneself, like being hung in mid-air, neither touching the sky above nor connected to the solid ground below, swaying, without any support. One cannot feel anything, and nothing can arouse interest, as if one is stiff and dead.

Encountering this kind of mood, only a cigarette can save it; nothing else seems to work. Smoke can stimulate one's nerves; smoke can revive a dead person. When a person is surrounded by the curling smoke, with eyes blurred, they can clear their mind. This sounds a bit strange, but it doesn't feel strange to say. Life is like light smoke, floating, floating, disappearing, and then the heart is disillusioned, dead. When one is in the midst of fragrant smoke, watching each smoke ring emerge from the throat, jump out from the bottom of the heart, then float upward, float upward; then the ring gradually expands; then it bursts; then the cigarette smoke hides towards the corner of the room, floats out the window, rises to the roof: in the air, the cigarette smoke is completely invisible, completely disappears; then the disillusioned mood suddenly realizes that life is also like light smoke: progressing from struggle, desperately climbing upward, radiating, then falling, then failing, then completely disappearing. People will wake up from this.

I don't know much about Buddhist principles, and I can't admire them with faith, but a novel called "Smoke" sometimes resonates with me. Although we are in the 20th century, we are far from the "smoke" era, our backgrounds are different, and our minds are different. However, the feeling of "smoke" can be tasted, because we are familiar with it, because we still sometimes share its power, because we are not completely separated from the "smoke" era, perhaps we cannot yet transcend the pre-"smoke" era?

I read "Smoke" many years ago, when I was too young and had too little life experience, so I didn't understand it very well. Now, I have entered "our world" for quite some time, so I climb, climb, then hit a wall, hit a wall; then I get stabbed; then I become disillusioned. Then, the smoke rings make me realize; then, "Smoke," which has been hidden in the corner of my mind for a long time, is recalled and resonated with. This may be the reason why Buddhism remains unchanged to this day, and why Buddhist principles are always studied and worshipped by people?

But, after waking up from the feeling of smoke, what then? Light another cigarette? Let the heart float, float again? Watch the smoke rings grow and disappear one by one again? This means, climb again in the world, climb, then fall again; then bear a body full of wounds again, climb again, fall again, fall and climb again, climb and fall again? People are really fools!

What is the "spirit of all things"? What is truly advanced humanity?

Look at the smoke again! You see it burning, burning, one smoke ring after another; one section of cigarette ash turns into embers, then another section of cigarette ash follows; the previous spark goes out, then the next spark follows. ... Then, the smoke is gone, the fire is completely extinguished, and a cigarette butt is thrown on the ground. On the ground, it burns, it still spits out strands of smoke, and then it is completely finished!

The smoke is gone, and the empty heart is no longer empty. The heart has gone through a journey from the moment the match lights the cigarette to the moment it is completely extinguished; the person has already experienced a week of life.

Then, the dream will suddenly wake up.

Are people really like smoke? Smoke will eventually disappear, but a second cigarette can follow. What about humanity? Humanity has sperm, history, books, axes, and machines.

Will the mood forever be immersed in smoke rings?

Night at Reed Sea 210

— Ai Tu

On the night I arrived in Changsha, my friends wanted to take me across the sea to Reed Sea. Of course, my mood was close to traveling, and I wouldn't miss going to a new place, especially since this is a very famous raw leaf market. It was even better for me.

After dinner, I followed my friends, hobbling out of the threshold of the towering building - this is the only famous school in Changsha. At that time, the setting sun still shone with a trace of light, turning Changsha Island from the sea to the quiet garden into a bleak and desolate red. Although this kind of brilliance is suitable for the senses of sad poets, I myself did not feel anything. After returning to the south this time, I had no interest in my home at all, and I didn't even want to go back for the two hours it would take. Such a chaotic family held no nostalgia for me. Therefore, after returning to the south, I still wandered as I did in Shanghai, without any sorrow lingering in my heart.

There, the desolate red of the setting sun shone broadly on the pond surface full of green lotus leaves, and also on the green leaves and bamboo forest by the pond. The reflected quiet appearance especially reminded me of the ghosts in a prison-like quiet countryside. However, I don't know what sentences those passionate poets and sad poets would use to depict it with their immortal pens?

We still loved a bit of childlike light noise, and talked and laughed as we first stepped onto the dock of Xinchang. The streets of Xinchang were already hung high with pale yellow electric lights, which was a warning of the coming of night! But! I was very happy, and while running on the not-so-popular cement road, I still dreamed of how to spend this night - because this night was too exciting for me, and I definitely wouldn't be able to sleep well. Therefore, I only hoped to be able to spend this quiet night on such a uniquely flavored street or on the dark sea.

We ran a lot from the west of Xinchang to the east, and the dim street lights still shone on us silently. When we arrived at the old dock for crossing the Reed Sea, I already felt the difference between two worlds.

The dock here is so dark! The uneven road is full of rubble, a bit like a beach. However, many, many people came and went here, all naturally and quickly. It made me feel too unfamiliar. I stepped onto a small boat. Look! On the other side is the street on the shore of Reed Sea, and the lights from the shops reflected on the clear water surface. When the slight waves rippled, the shadows of the lights also rippled at the bottom of the sea, from clear to hazy. In the distance, the gray or white walls made people believe that this semi-new and semi-old town was a good place for war. In the sky, the dark blue, bright sparse stars twinkled and revealed their lovely brilliance. Therefore, they were also reflected in the sea, like countless small lamps. A half-curved moon hid in the gray, light clouds like a shy girl. The boat swayed on the sea, and the light waves also undulated, so we believed even more that the moon had fallen into the deep sea and was shaking.

When we arrived at the streets of Reed Sea, it was no different from other cities, and the place was not small. There were also many people coming and going. Indeed, this small port was the most lively. There were many street vendors and peddlers. This is a prosperous area in the southwest corner of Taishan, so at night, it's a bit like a "city that never sleeps."

However, the liveliness or lack thereof of the streets didn't give me much feeling or nostalgia. Therefore, after running enough, we bought some sweets and stepped onto the small boat again. At this time, we really wanted to have an interesting night boat ride on the sea.

The sea at Reed Sea was so calm! It seemed that the universe had been buried in a dead garden. All we heard were the sounds of oars and water. The moon in the sky was even more hazy. We knew that it was already very late, and the boatman also wanted to sleep. So, quietly, we turned towards the dock of our home.

Song Introduction 211

Begging Song

Autumn winds rise, autumn clouds fly, pieces of fallen leaves flutter all over the ground. Looking far at the boundless sky, only a group of lost swallows can be seen, wandering and flying in all directions! Alas! They are displaced from their homes, living without a fixed place and without warm clothes. Their huts are all washed away; their flesh and blood are separated. They can only bitterly beg for food while fleeing from the famine. How can they avoid the wind and rain, their bodies cold and their bellies hungry? They are truly lacking clothes and food, with no one to turn to!

The disaster victims are cold, the disaster victims are hungry, one by one crying and weeping. When the cold north wind rises, they will helplessly await death, gasping for breath! Dying, dying like insects! Compatriots! They are like wild dogs, no one to care for them, no one to pity them. Who has no brothers, who has no sisters? It is pitiful that they are wandering in ditches, relying entirely on your enthusiastic relief, and your generous donations. Donating a penny saves a life, and the merit is boundless!

Storytelling with Stringed Instruments 212

Xing Ruiting's Hairpin Phoenix

Huiling (1380) 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening: "Longevity Character"

The longevity star is as brilliant as the planet Venus. It hangs in the southern sky. Longevity candles burn high, their red shadows flickering. Close relatives and friends wish the old man longevity. His descendants have been prosperous for five generations, immeasurable. Fruits, noodles, peaches, and cakes fill the table. Only to see that. His longevity is as long as the sky, like pine and crane. This beautiful story is wished to the longevity old man. Longevity couplets, all kinds are even. They hang on both pillars. Able to make the old man happy. A feast is set up, and wine is poured frequently. The old man originally has boundless joy. Guests fill the door, and a festive atmosphere arises. Only feels the longevity hall is very lively. Stringed instruments and flutes. Double stars shine brightly in the hall. Adorning the splendor of the longevity candles. The wonderful appearance is exquisite and colorful. Dragons embroidered with bright colors. Together ascend to the realm of longevity. Enjoy longevity, long and eternal. You don't see. Guo Ziyi's longevity was originally invincible. The hundred-year-old man is refreshed. Passing leisurely years. Longevity is like green pine, with an immortal name. Now. Western Sichuan's longevity is forever. Can be called the longevity of the world without stealing. He. Was born in the early Qing Dynasty and enjoyed a long life. More than two hundred years is really not light. His steps are as swift as flying, and his energy is strong. Clear spirit and refreshing hidden wilderness city. Who in the world knows the method of old age? All rely on self-cultivation to prolong life. Therefore, people should cultivate their breath. Enjoy longevity and long life. Otherwise, how can one obtain old age? Ending their short life will lead to death. Glory and wealth collapse one morning.

Movies

A Romance in "Triumphant Song" 214

In the "Triumphant Song" produced by Yihua Company and directed by Bu Wancang, Wang Yin and Yuan Meiyun play a pair of cousins who are in love.

On a very poetic evening, the two of them walked side by side from one side of the field, Meiyun carrying a water chestnut basket in her hand, and Wang Yin carrying an iron hoe on his shoulder.

The surroundings were quiet, and the evening scenery of the countryside could not have been better. The two of them talked and laughed while walking, and the scene seemed particularly intimate.

Suddenly, Wang Yin stopped and said to Meiyun: "Sister Guiying, I won't see you off anymore, I haven't gone home yet!" Ah! How sweet that voice is!

"Thank you, Brother Chunsheng, for walking so far with me." Ah! How sweet that voice is too!

"What are you saying? You can invite me to eat a few more water chestnuts later."

"Okay! Definitely."

The two of them finally separated and went home, but what exactly was the reluctance when they left? This is only for you to see in "Triumphant Song."

Silver Moon Prepares for Large-Scale Performance 215

The Silver Moon Dance Troupe, organized by dance expert Ms. Zhang Qing'e, has been performing in various parts of South China since last winter, for a period of one year. Famous in the South, renowned in Fujian and Guangdong, among the major dance troupes that have emerged in recent years, Silver Moon is undoubtedly the best. It has now returned to Shanghai. Silver Moon is known for Feng Feng, Jin Yu, Xu Lingling, and Wu Dieying. In terms of dance skills, they are better than the so-called song and dance stars of today. After returning to Shanghai, they immediately devoted themselves to practice, without taking a moment's rest. Their spirit of diligence and hard work is rare in the song and dance world. It is no wonder that they want to cause a sensation on the red carpet. The troupe plans to give a large-scale performance in this city once special programs have been fully rehearsed.

Cai Chusheng's new work "Lost Lamb" will use a relaxed approach to write about extremely serious issues.

In order to make it easier for Shang Guanwu to come to the company, he has now moved to Xujiahui.

Huahua Drama Club Recruits Male and Female Actors 217

Since the Huahua Drama Club in this city performed, it once recruited actors last month. There were many applicants, and two were immediately admitted, one was Ms. Shen Yan from the Lihua Drama Troupe in Beiping, and the other was the newcomer Gu Feng, (namely Yao Yaying). Recently, in order to enrich its lineup, the club will continue to recruit male and female actors, regardless of age. Those who are admitted will be provided with food and lodging. The qualifications must include literary cultivation and the ability to speak Mandarin. Those interested can sign up at 576 Laoshunfu Road in the French Concession.

Publishing Industry 218

The resumed issue of *Dianying Xinwen* (电影新闻), edited by Han Pingye, was published yesterday. The cover is printed in two-color edition. There are a total of twenty celebrity photos, and the manuscripts are extremely appropriate. There are five special news items that other film publications have not been able to fully know. The film news within a week is also comprehensive. There are also interesting and spicy film anecdotes such as "It's About That," and Mr. Hou Ping's film realism novel "The Amorous Tofu Exhibition," the first issue of which is "Sentimental Love Song," which is written with people and is vivid and lively. It will be loved by the general public. Each volume is only sold for five cents of ocean. Shanghai Magazine Company on the Fourth Road in Shanghai is the general distributor, and all bookstores and news vendors are for sale.
